Page 1
Iran 
Coordinates: [URL: "https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Iran&params=32_N_53_E_dim:1000km_type:country_region:IR"] 32°N 53°E
Iran (Persian: ‎ایران Irân [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian"] [ʔiːˈɾɒːn] (  listen)),  also called
Persia,[11] and officially the Islamic Republic of Iran,[a] is a
country in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Asia"] Western Asia. It is bordered by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq"] Iraq and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey"] Turkey to the
 west, by Azerbaijan and Armenia to the northwest, by the Caspian
Sea and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmenistan"] Turkmenistan to the north, by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan"] Afghanistan and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan"] Pakistan to
the east, and by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman"] Gulf of Oman and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf"] Persian Gulf to the south.
It covers an area of 1,648,195 km2 (636,372 sq mi), making it the
 fourth-largest country entirely in Asia and the second-largest
country in Western Asia behind [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia"] Saudi Arabia. Iran has a population
of 85 million, making it the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population"] 17th-most populous country in the
world.[12] Its capital and largest city is Tehran, followed by
Mashhad, Isfahan, Karaj, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shiraz"] Shiraz and Tabriz.
The country is home to one of the world's  oldest
civilizations,[13][14] beginning with the formation of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elam"] Elamite
kingdoms in the fourth millennium BC. It was first unified by the
Medes, an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_ancient_Iranian_peoples"] ancient Iranian people, in the seventh century BC,[15]
and reached its territorial height in the sixth century BC, when
 Cyrus the Great founded the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Persian Empire, which
became [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_empires"] one of the largest empires in history and has been described
as the world's first effective superpower.[16] The Achaemenid
Empire fell to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great"] Alexander the Great in the fourth century BC and
was subsequently divided into several [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period"] Hellenistic states. An Iranian
rebellion established the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire"] Parthian Empire in the third century BC,
 which was succeeded in the third century AD by the Sassanid
Empire, a major world power for the next four centuries.[17][18]
 Arab Muslims conquered the empire in the seventh century AD,
which led to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization_of_Iran"] Islamization of Iran. It subsequently became a
major center of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_culture"] Islamic culture and learning, with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_art"] its art, literature,
philosophy, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_architecture"] architecture spreading across the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world"] Muslim world and
beyond during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age"] Islamic Golden Age. Over the next two
centuries, a series of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Intermezzo"] native Iranian Muslim dynasties emerged
before the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_dynasty"] Seljuk Turks and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilkhanate"] Mongols conquered the region. In
the 15th century, the native [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_dynasty"] Safavids re-established a unified Iranian
 state and national identity,[4] and converted the country to Shia
Islam.[5][19] Under the reign of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah"] Nader Shah in the 18th century, Iran
once again became a major world power,[20] though by the 19th
century, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars"] series of conflicts with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire"] Russian Empire led to
significant territorial losses.[21][22] The early 20th century saw the
 Persian Constitutional Revolution. Efforts to nationalize its fossil
 fuel supply from Western companies led to an Anglo-American
coup in 1953, which resulted in greater autocratic rule under
 Mohammad Reza Pahlavi and growing Western political
influence.[23] He went on to launch [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Revolution"] a far-reaching series of reforms
 in 1963.[24] After the Iranian Revolution, the current Islamic
Republic was established in 1979[25] by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini"] Ruhollah Khomeini, who
became the country's first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran"] Supreme Leader.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] government of Iran is an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_theocracy"] Islamic theocracy that includes
elements of a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system"] presidential democracy, with the ultimate authority
 vested in an autocratic "Supreme Leader";[26] a position held by Ali
Khamenei since Khomeini's death in 1989. The Iranian government

Page 2
is widely considered to be authoritarian, and has attracted
widespread criticism for its significant constraints and abuses against
 human rights and civil liberties,[27][28][29][30] including several
 violent suppressions of mass protests, unfair elections, and limited
 rights for women and for children. It is also a focal point for Shia
Islam within the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East"] Middle East, countering the long-existing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs"] Arab and
 Sunni hegemony within the region. Since the Iranian Revolution,
the country is widely considered to be the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict"] largest adversary of Israel
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_proxy_conflict"] also of Saudi Arabia. Iran is also considered to be one of the
biggest players within Middle Eastern affairs, with its government
being involved both directly and indirectly in the majority of
 modern Middle Eastern conflicts.
Iran is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power"] regional and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_power"] middle power, with a geopolitically strategic
location in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia"] Asian continent.[31] It is a founding member of the
 United Nations, the ECO, the OIC, and the OPEC. It has large
 reserves of fossil fuels—including the second-largest natural gas
supply and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves"] fourth-largest proven oil reserves.[32] The country's
 rich cultural legacy is reflected in part by its 26 UNESCO World
Heritage Sites.[33] Historically a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multinational_state"] multinational state, Iran remains a
 pluralistic society comprising numerous ethnic, linguistic, and
religious groups, with the largest of these being Persians, Azeris,
Kurds, Mazandaranis, and Lurs.[3]

Name
The term [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_(word)"] Iran derives directly from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Persian"] Middle Persian Ērān, first attested in a
third-century inscription at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naqsh-e_Rostam"] Naqsh-e Rostam, with the accompanying [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_language"] Parthian
 inscription using the term Aryān, in reference to the Iranians.[36] The Middle
Iranian ērān and aryān are oblique plural forms of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demonym"] gentilic nouns ēr- (Middle
Persian) and ary- (Parthian), both deriving from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Iranian_language"] Proto-Iranian language *arya-
(meaning "Aryan", i.e. "of the Iranians"),[36][37] recognized as a derivative of
 Proto-Indo-European language *ar-yo-,  meaning "one who assembles
(skilfully)".[38] In the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_languages"] Iranian languages, the gentilic is attested as a self-
identifier, included in ancient inscriptions and the literature of the Avesta,[39][b]
and remains also in other Iranian ethnic names [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alans"] Alan (Ossetian: Ир Ir) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_people"] Iron
(Ирон).[37] According to the Iranian mythology, the country's name comes
from the name of Iraj, a legendary prince and shah who was killed by his
brothers.[40]Historically, Iran has been referred to as Persia by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world"] the West,[11]
due mainly to the writings of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greeks"] Greek historians who referred to all of Iran as 
Inscription of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardashir_I"] Ardeshir Babakan (r. 224–
242) in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahura_Mazda_and_Ardashir_I"] Naqsh-e Rostam: "This is the
figure of Mazdaworshiper, the lord
Ardashir, Shahanshah of Iran..."[34]
Persís ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek"] Ancient Greek: Περσίς; from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Persian"] Old Persian  Pârsa),[41]
meaning "land of the Persians", while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persis"] Persis itself was one of the provinces of ancient Iran that is today known as Fars.[42]
As the most extensive interaction the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece"] ancient Greeks had with any outsider was with the Persians, the term persisted, even
long after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars"] Greco-Persian Wars (499–449 BC).
Page 4
In 1935, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Shah"] Reza Shah requested the international community to refer to the
country by its native name, Iran, on Nowruz, falling on 21 March 1935;
effective 22 March that year.[43][44] Opposition to the name change led to the
reversal of the decision in 1959, and Professor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ehsan_Yarshater"] Ehsan Yarshater, editor of
 Encyclopædia Iranica,  propagated a move to use Persia and Iran
interchangeably.[45] Today, both Iran and Persia are used in cultural contexts,
while Iran remains irreplaceable in official state contexts.[46]
Historical and cultural usage of the word Iran is not restricted to the modern
state proper.[47][48][49] "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Iran"] Greater Iran" (Irānzamīn or Irān e Bozorg)[50] refers to
territories of the Iranian cultural and linguistic zones. In addition to modern
Iran, it includes portions of the Caucasus, Anatolia, Mesopotamia, Afghanistan,
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia.[51] 
An [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashrafi"] Ashrafi Coin of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah"] Nader Shah (r. 1736–
1747), reverse:"Coined on gold the word of
 kingdom in the world, Nader of Greater
Iran and the world-conquerer king."[35]
Pronunciation
The Persian pronunciation of Iran is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian"] [ʔiːˈɾɒːn]. Common [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_in_the_Commonwealth_of_Nations"] Commonwealth English pronunciations of Iran are listed in the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary"] Oxford English Dictionary as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈrɑːn/ and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈræn/,[52] while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English"] American English dictionaries such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merriam-Webster"] Merriam-Webster's
 provide pronunciations which map to /ɪˈrɑːn, -ˈræn, aɪˈræn/,[53] or likewise in Random House Webster's Unabridged
Dictionary as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈræn, ɪˈrɑːn, aɪˈræn/. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambridge_Advanced_Learner%27s_Dictionary"] Cambridge Dictionary lists [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈrɑːn/ as the British pronunciation and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈræn/ as the
American pronunciation. Similarly, Glasgow-based [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collins_English_Dictionary"] Collins English Dictionary provides both [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language_in_England"] English English and
American English pronunciations. The pronunciation guide from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voice_of_America"] Voice of America also provides [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈrɑːn/.[54]
The American English pronunciation [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /aɪˈræn/ may be heard in U.S. media. Max Fisher in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post"] The Washington Post[55]
prescribed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /iːˈrɑːn/ for Iran, while proscribing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /aɪˈræn/. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_American_Heritage_Dictionary_of_the_English_Language"] The American Heritage Dictionary of the English Language, in the
dictionary's 2014 Usage Ballot, addressed the topic of the pronunciations of Iran and Iraq.[56] According to this survey, the
pronunciations [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈrɑːn/ and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈræn/ were deemed almost equally acceptable, while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /ɪˈrɑːn/ was preferred by most panelists
participating in the ballot. With regard to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /aɪˈræn/ pronunciation, more than 70% of the panelists deemed it unacceptable.
Among the reasons given by those panelists were that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /aɪˈræn/ has "hawkish connotations" and sounds "angrier",
"xenophobic", "ignorant", and "not ... cosmopolitan". The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English"] /aɪˈræn/ pronunciation remains standard and acceptable, reflected
in the entry for Iran in the American Heritage Dictionary itself, as well as in each of the other major dictionaries of
American English.
History
Prehistory
The earliest attested archaeological artifacts in Iran, like those excavated at
 Kashafrud and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganj_Par"] Ganj Par in northern Iran, confirm a human presence in Iran since
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic"] Lower Paleolithic.[58] Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal"] Neanderthal artifacts from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic"] Middle Paleolithic
have been found mainly in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zagros_Mountains"] Zagros region, at sites such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warwasi"] Warwasi and
Yafteh.[59][60] From the 10th to the seventh millennium BC, early agricultural
communities began to flourish in and around the Zagros region in western Iran,
 including Chogha Golan,[61][62] Chogha Bonut,[63][64] and Chogha
Mish.[65][66][67] 
A [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cave_painting"] cave painting in Doushe cave,
The occupation of grouped hamlets in the area of Susa, as determined by
 radiocarbon dating, ranges from 4395–3955 to 3680–3490 BC.[68] There are 
Lorestan, from the 8th millennium
BC[57]
dozens of prehistoric sites across the Iranian Plateau, pointing to the existence of
ancient cultures and urban settlements in the fourth millennium BC.[67][69][70] During the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronze_Age"] Bronze Age, the territory of
present-day Iran was home to several civilizations, including Elam, Jiroft, and Zayanderud. Elam, the most prominent of
these civilizations, developed in the southwest alongside those in Mesopotamia, and continued its existence until the
emergence of the Iranian empires. The advent of writing in Elam was paralleled to Sumer, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elamite_cuneiform"] Elamite cuneiform was
developed since the third millennium BC.[71]
Page 5
From the 34th to the 20th century BC, northwestern Iran was part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kura-Araxes_culture"] Kura-Araxes culture, which stretched into the
neighboring [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus"] Caucasus and Anatolia. Since the earliest second millennium BC, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyria"] Assyrians settled in swaths of western Iran
and incorporated the region into their territories.
Classical antiquity
By the second millennium BC, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_ancient_Iranian_peoples"] ancient Iranian peoples arrived in what is now
Iran from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_Steppe"] Eurasian Steppe,[72] rivaling the native settlers of the region.[73][74]
As the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_peoples"] Iranians dispersed into the wider area of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Iran"] Greater Iran and beyond, the
boundaries of modern-day Iran were dominated by Median, Persian, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthia"] Parthian
tribes.
From the late 10th to the late seventh century BC, the Iranian peoples, together with
the "pre-Iranian" kingdoms, fell under the domination of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyria"] Assyrian Empire,
based in northern Mesopotamia.[75] Under king Cyaxares, the Medes and Persians
entered into an alliance with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia"] Babylonian ruler Nabopolassar, as well as the fellow 
A [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relief#Bas-relief_or_low_relief"] bas-relief at Persepolis, depicting
the united [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medes"] Medes and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persians"] Persians
Iranian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scythians"] Scythians and Cimmerians, and together they attacked the Assyrian Empire.
The civil war ravaged the Assyrian Empire between 616 and 605 BC, thus freeing their respective peoples from three
centuries of Assyrian rule.[75] The unification of the Median tribes under king [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deioces"] Deioces in 728 BC led to the foundation of
the Median Empire which, by 612 BC, controlled almost the entire territory of present-day Iran and eastern Anatolia.[76]
This marked the end of the Kingdom of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urartu"] Urartu as well, which was subsequently conquered and dissolved.[77][78]
In 550 BC, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great"] Cyrus the Great, the son of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandane_of_Media"] Mandane and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambyses_I"] Cambyses I, took over the
Median Empire, and founded the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire by unifying other city-states.
The conquest of Media was a result of what is called the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Revolt"] Persian Revolt.  The
 brouhaha was initially triggered by the actions of the Median ruler Astyages, and
was quickly spread to other provinces as they allied with the Persians. Later
conquests under Cyrus and his successors expanded the empire to include Lydia,
Babylon, Egypt, parts of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans"] Balkans and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Europe"] Eastern Europe proper, as well as the
lands to the west of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_River"] Indus and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amu_Darya"] Oxus rivers.
539 BC was the year in which Persian forces defeated the Babylonian army at Opis,
and marked the end of around four centuries of Mesopotamian domination of the
region by conquering the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire"] Neo-Babylonian Empire. Cyrus entered Babylon and
presented himself as a traditional Mesopotamian monarch. Subsequent Achaemenid
art and iconography reflect the influence of the new political reality in Mesopotamia. 
 Tomb of Cyrus the Great, founder of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire, in
 Pasargadae
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire (550 BC–
 330 BC) around the time of Darius
the Great and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xerxes_I"] Xerxes I 
At its greatest extent, the Achaemenid Empire included territories of modern-day
Iran, Republic of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan"] Azerbaijan ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arran_(Caucasus)"] Arran and Shirvan),  Armenia, Georgia, Turkey
(Anatolia),  much of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea"] Black Sea coastal regions, northeastern Greece and
southern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria"] Bulgaria (Thrace), northern Greece and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Macedonia"] North Macedonia ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paeonia_(kingdom)"] Paeonia and
Macedon), Iraq, Syria, Lebanon, Jordan, Israel and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_territories"] Palestinian territories, all
significant population centers of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt"] ancient Egypt as far west as Libya, Kuwait,
northern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia"] Saudi Arabia, parts of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates"] United Arab Emirates and Oman, Pakistan,
Afghanistan, and much of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia, making it the largest empire the world had
yet seen.[16]
It is estimated that in 480 BC, 50 million people lived in the Achaemenid
Empire.[79][80] The empire at its peak ruled over 44% of the world's population, the
highest such figure for any empire in history.[81]
The Achaemenid Empire is noted for the release of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonian_captivity"] Jewish exiles in Babylon,[82] building infrastructures such as the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Road"] Royal Road and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chapar_Khaneh"] Chapar (postal service),  and the use of an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language"] official language, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Aramaic#Imperial_Aramaic"] Imperial Aramaic, throughout its
territories.[16] The empire had a centralized, bureaucratic administration under the emperor, a large professional army, and
civil services, inspiring similar developments in later empires.[83][84]
Eventual conflict on the western borders began with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionian_Revolt"] Ionian Revolt, which erupted into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars"] Greco-Persian Wars and
continued through the first half of the fifth century BC, and ended with the withdrawal of the Achaemenids from all of the
territories in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans"] Balkans and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Europe"] Eastern Europe proper.[85]
Page 6
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire"] Parthian Empire (247 BC–224
AD) in 94 BC at its greatest extent,
during the reign of Mithridates II 
In 334 BC, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great"] Alexander the Great invaded the Achaemenid Empire, defeating the last
Achaemenid emperor, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_III"] Darius III, at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Issus"] Battle of Issus. Following the premature
death of Alexander, Iran came under the control of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period"] Hellenistic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seleucid_Empire"] Seleucid Empire.
In the middle of the second century BC, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire"] Parthian Empire rose to become the
main power in Iran, and the century-long geopolitical arch-rivalry between the
Romans and the Parthians began, culminating in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Parthian_Wars"] Roman–Parthian Wars. The
Parthian Empire continued as a feudal monarchy for nearly five centuries, until
224 CE, when it was succeeded by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire"] Sasanian Empire.[86] Together with their
neighboring arch-rival, the Roman-Byzantines, they made up the world's two most
dominant powers at the time, for over four centuries.[17][18]
The Sasanians established an empire within the frontiers achieved by the
Achaemenids, with their capital at Ctesiphon. Late antiquity is considered one of Iran's most influential periods, as under the
Sasanians their influence reached the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_ancient_Rome"] culture of ancient Rome (and through that as far as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe"] Western Europe),[87][88]
Africa,[89] China, and India,[90] and played a prominent role in the formation of the medieval art of both [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_art"] Europe and
Asia.[91]
Most of the era of the Sasanian Empire was overshadowed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars"] Roman–Persian Wars, which raged on the western
borders at Anatolia, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Caucasus"] Western Caucasus, Mesopotamia, and the Levant, for over 700 years. These wars ultimately
exhausted both the Romans and the Sasanians and led to the defeat of both by the Muslim invasion.
Throughout the Achaemenid, Parthian, and Sasanian eras, several offshoots of the Iranian dynasties established [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eponym"] eponymous
branches in Anatolia and the Caucasus, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Pontus"] Pontic Kingdom, the Mihranids, and the Arsacid dynasties of
Armenia, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arsacid_dynasty_of_Iberia"] Iberia (Georgia), and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arsacid_dynasty_of_Caucasian_Albania"] Caucasian Albania (present-day Republic of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan"] Azerbaijan and southern Dagestan).
Medieval period
 The prolonged Byzantine–Sasanian wars, most importantly the climactic war of 602–628, as well as the social conflict
within the Sasanian Empire, opened the way for an Arab invasion of Iran in the seventh century.[92][93] The empire was
 initially defeated by the Rashidun Caliphate, which was succeeded by the Umayyad Caliphate, followed by the Abbasid
Caliphate. A prolonged and gradual process of state-imposed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization_of_Iran"] Islamization followed, which targeted Iran's then Zoroastrian
majority and included religious persecution,[94][95][96] demolition of libraries[97] and fire temples,[98] a special tax penalty
("jizya"),[99][100] and language shift.[101][102]
In 750, the Abbasids overthrew the Umayyads.[103] Arabs Muslims and Persians of all strata made up the rebel army, which
was united by the converted Persian Muslim, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Muslim"] Abu Muslim.[104][105][106] In their struggle for power, the society in their
times gradually became cosmopolitan and the old Arab simplicity and aristocratic dignity, bearing and prestige were lost.
Persians and Turks began to replace the Arabs in most fields. The fusion of the Arab nobility with the subject races, the
practice of polygamy and concubinage, made for a social amalgam wherein loyalties became uncertain and a hierarchy of
officials emerged, a bureaucracy at first Persian and later Turkish which decreased Abbasid prestige and power for
good.[107]
After two centuries of Arab rule, semi-independent and independent Iranian kingdoms—including the Tahirids, Saffarids,
Samanids, and Buyids—began to appear on the fringes of the declining Abbasid Caliphate.
The blossoming literature, philosophy, mathematics, medicine, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age#Astronomy"] astronomy and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_art"] art of Iran became major elements in the
formation of a new age for the Iranian civilization, during a period known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age"] Islamic Golden Age.[111][112] The Islamic
Golden Age reached its peak by the 10th and 11th centuries, during which Iran was the main theater of scientific
activities.[113]
The cultural revival that began in the Abbasid period led to a resurfacing of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_nationalism"] Iranian national identity; thus, the attempts
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabization"] Arabization never succeeded in Iran. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shu%27ubiyya"] Shu'ubiyya movement became a catalyst for Iranians to regain independence in
their relations with the Arab invaders.[114] The most notable effect of this movement was the continuation of the Persian
language attested to the works of the epic poet Ferdowsi, now considered the most prominent figure in Iranian literature.
The 10th century saw a mass migration of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_tribal_confederations"] Turkic tribes from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia into the Iranian Plateau.[115] Turkic tribesmen
were first used in the Abbasid army as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamluk"] mamluks (slave-warriors), replacing Iranian and Arab elements within the army.[104]
As a result, the Mamluks gained significant political power. In 999, large portions of Iran came briefly under the rule of the
Ghaznavids, whose rulers were of mamluk Turkic origin, and longer subsequently under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuk_Empire"] Seljuk and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anushtegin_dynasty"] Khwarezmian
Page 7
empires.[115] The Seljuks subsequently gave rise to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum"] Sultanate of Rum in
Anatolia, while taking their thoroughly Persianized identity with them.[116][117] The
result of the adoption and patronage of Persian culture by Turkish rulers was the
development of a distinct [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turco-Persian_tradition"] Turco-Persian tradition.
 From 1219 to 1221, under the Khwarazmian Empire, Iran suffered a devastating
invasion by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire"] Mongol Empire army of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genghis_Khan"] Genghis Khan. According to Steven R.
Ward, "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests"] Mongol violence and depredations killed up to three-fourths of the
population of the Iranian Plateau, possibly 10 to 15 million people. Some historians
have estimated that Iran's population did not again reach its pre-Mongol levels until
the mid-20th century."[118] Most modern historians either outright dismiss or are
highly skeptical of such statistics of colossal magnitude pertaining the Mongol
onslaught on the Khwarazmian empire, mainland Iran and other Muslim regions
and deem them to be exaggerations by Muslim chroniclers of that era (whose
recordings were naturally of an anti-Mongol bent). Indeed, as far as the Iranian
plateau was concerned, the bulk of the Mongol onslaught and battles were in the
northeast of what is modern-day Iran. Such as the cities of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nishapur"] Nishapur and
Tus.[119][120][121] 
 Tomb of Hafez, a medieval Persian
poet whose works are regarded as a
pinnacle in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_literature"] Persian literature and
have left a considerable mark on
later Western writers, most notably
 Johann Wolfgang von Goethe, Henry
David Thoreau, and
 Emerson[108][109][110]
Following the fracture of the Mongol Empire in 1256, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulagu_Khan"] Hulagu Khan, grandson of Genghis Khan, established the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilkhanate"] Ilkhanate
in Iran. In 1370, yet another conqueror, Timur, followed the example of Hulagu, establishing the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_Empire"] Timurid Empire which
lasted for another 156 years. In 1387, Timur ordered the complete massacre of Isfahan, reportedly killing 70,000
citizens.[122] The Ilkhans and the Timurids soon came to adopt the ways and customs of the Iranians, surrounding
themselves with a culture that was distinctively Iranian.[123]
Early modern period
Safavids
By the 1500s, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_I"] Ismail I of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardabil"] Ardabil established the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_Iran"] Safavid Empire,[124] with his capital at
Tabriz.[115] Beginning with Azerbaijan, he subsequently extended his authority over all of
the Iranian territories, and established an intermittent Iranian hegemony over the vast relative
regions, reasserting the Iranian identity within large parts of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Iran"] Greater Iran.[125] Iran was
predominantly Sunni,[126] but Ismail instigated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_conversion_of_Iran_to_Shia_Islam"] a forced conversion to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shia branch of
Islam,[127] spreading throughout the Safavid territories in the Caucasus, Iran, Anatolia, and
Mesopotamia. As a result, modern-day Iran is the only official Shia nation of the world,
with it holding an absolute majority in Iran and the Republic of Azerbaijan, having there the
first and the second highest number of Shia inhabitants by population percentage in the
world.[128][129] Meanwhile, the centuries-long geopolitical and ideological rivalry between
 Safavid Iran and the neighboring Ottoman Empire led to numerous Ottoman–Iranian
wars.[118]
The Safavid era peaked in the reign of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_the_Great"] Abbas I (1587–1629),[118][130] surpassing their 
 Venetian portrait, kept at the
Uffizi, of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_I"] Ismail I, the
 founder of the Safavid
Turkish archrivals in strength, and making Iran a leading science and art hub in western Empire
Eurasia. The Safavid era saw the start of mass integration from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus"] Caucasian populations into
new layers of the society of Iran, as well as mass resettlement of them within the heartlands
of Iran, playing a pivotal role in the history of Iran for centuries onwards. Following a gradual decline in the late 1600s and
the early 1700s, which was caused by internal conflicts, the continuous wars with the Ottomans, and the foreign
interference (most notably the Russian interference), the Safavid rule was ended by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hotak_dynasty"] Pashtun rebels who besieged Isfahan
and defeated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultan_Husayn"] Sultan Husayn in 1722.
Afsharids
In 1729, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah"] Nader Shah, a chieftain and military genius from Khorasan, successfully drove out and conquered the Pashtun
invaders. He subsequently took back the annexed Caucasian territories which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Constantinople_(1724)"] were divided among the Ottoman and
 Russian authorities by the ongoing chaos in Iran. During the reign of Nader Shah, Iran reached its greatest extent since the
Page 8
Sasanian Empire, reestablishing the Iranian hegemony all over the Caucasus, as well as
other major parts of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia"] west and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] central Asia, and briefly possessing what was arguably the
most powerful empire at the time.[20]
Nader Shah [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah%27s_invasion_of_the_Mughal_Empire"] invaded India and sacked far off Delhi
by the late 1730s. His territorial expansion, as well
as his military successes, went into a decline
 following the final campaigns in the Northern
Caucasus against then revolting Lezgins. The
assassination of Nader Shah sparked a brief period
of civil war and turmoil, after which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karim_Khan_Zand"] Karim Khan of
A portrait of Abbas I, the
powerful, pragmatic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_dynasty"] Safavid
ruler who reinforced Iran's
military, political, and 
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zand_dynasty"] Zand dynasty came to power in 1750, bringing a
period of relative peace and prosperity.[118]
Zands 
Statue of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nader_Shah"] Nader Shah, the first
 Afsharid ruler of Iran, at his [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomb_of_Nader_Shah"] Tomb
economic power  Compared to its preceding dynasties, the geopolitical reach of the Zand dynasty was limited.
Many of the Iranian territories in the Caucasus gained de facto autonomy and were locally
ruled through various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanates_of_the_Caucasus"] Caucasian khanates. However, despite the self-ruling, they all
remained [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commoner"] subjects and vassals to the Zand king.[131] Another civil war ensued after the death of Karim Khan in 1779, out of
which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agha_Mohammad_Khan_Qajar"] Agha Mohammad Khan emerged, founding the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty"] Qajar dynasty in 1794.
Qajars
In 1795, following the disobedience of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgians"] Georgian subjects and their [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Georgievsk"] alliance with the Russians, the Qajars captured
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tbilisi"] Tbilisi by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Krtsanisi"] Battle of Krtsanisi, and drove the Russians out of the entire Caucasus, reestablishing the Iranian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suzerainty"] suzerainty
over the region. 
The Russo-Iranian wars of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)"] 1804–1813 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%9328)"] 1826–1828 resulted in large irrevocable
territorial losses for Iran in the Caucasus, comprising all of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Caucasus"] South Caucasus and
Dagestan, which made part of the very concept of Iran for centuries,[21] and thus
substantial gains for the neighboring Russian Empire.
As a result of the 19th-century Russo-Iranian wars, the Russians took over the
Caucasus, and Iran irrevocably lost control over its integral territories in the region
 (comprising modern-day Dagestan, Georgia, Armenia, and Republic of

northwestern borders of Iran,
comprising modern-day eastern
Georgia, Dagestan, Armenia, and the 
Azerbaijan),  which got confirmed per the treaties of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan"] Gulistan and
Turkmenchay.[22][132] The area to the north of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aras_(river)"] Aras River, among which the
contemporary Republic of Azerbaijan, eastern Georgia, Dagestan, and Armenia are
located, were Iranian territory until they were occupied by Russia in the course of
the 19th century.[22][133][134][135][136][137][138]
 Republic of Azerbaijan, before being
 ceded to the neighboring Russian
Empire by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars"] Russo-Iranian wars 
As Iran shrank, many [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Caucasus"] South Caucasian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Caucasus"] North Caucasian Muslims moved
 towards Iran,[139][140] especially until the aftermath of the Circassian
Genocide,[140] and the decades afterwards, while Iran's  Armenians were
encouraged to settle in the newly incorporated Russian territories,[141][142][143]
causing significant demographic shifts.
Around 1.5 million people—20 to 25% of the population of Iran—died as a result of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_famine_of_1870-1872"] Great Famine of 1870–1872.[144]
Between 1872 and 1905, a series of protests took place in response to the sale of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concession_(contract)"] concessions to foreigners by Qajar
 monarchs Naser-ed-Din and Mozaffar-ed-Din, and led to the Constitutional Revolution in 1905. The first Iranian
constitution and the first national parliament of Iran were founded in 1906, through the ongoing revolution. The
Constitution included the official recognition of Iran's three religious minorities, namely Christians, Jews, and
Zoroastrians,[145] which has remained a basis in the legislation of Iran since then. The struggle related to the constitutional
movement was followed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triumph_of_Tehran"] Triumph of Tehran in 1909, when [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Ali_Shah_Qajar"] Mohammad Ali Shah was defeated and forced to
abdicate. On the pretext of restoring order, the Russians occupied northern Iran in 1911 and maintained a military presence
 in the region for years to come. But this did not put an end to the civil uprisings and was soon followed by Mirza Kuchik
Khan's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungle_Movement_of_Gilan"] Jungle Movement against both the Qajar monarchy and foreign invaders.

Despite Iran's neutrality during [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I"] World War I, the
Ottoman, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire"] Russian and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire"] British empires occupied the
 territory of western Iran and fought the Persian
Campaign before fully withdrawing their forces in
1921. At least 2 million Persian civilians died either
 directly in the fighting, the Ottoman perpetrated
 anti-Christian genocides or the war-induced famine
of 1917-1919. A large number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Assyrian"] Iranian Assyrian
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Armenian"] Iranian Armenian Christians, as well as those
Muslims who tried to protect them, were victims of
 mass murders committed by the invading Ottoman
troops, notably in and around Khoy, Maku, Salmas,
and Urmia.[146][147][148][149][150] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baharestan"] first national Iranian Parliament
was established in 1906 during the
 Persian Constitutional Revolution
Apart from the rule of Agha Mohammad Khan, the Qajar rule is characterized as a century
of misrule.[115] The inability of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_Iran"] Qajar Iran's government to maintain the country's
 sovereignty during and immediately after World War I led to the British directed 1921
Persian coup d'état and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Shah"] Reza Shah's establishment of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pahlavi_dynasty"] Pahlavi dynasty. Reza Shah,
became the new [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Iran"] Prime Minister of Iran and was declared the new monarch in 1925.
Pahlavis
 In the midst of World War II, in June 1941, Nazi Germany broke the Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact and invaded the Soviet
Union, Iran's northern neighbor. The Soviets quickly allied themselves with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II"] Allied countries and in July and August,
1941 the British demanded that the Iranian government expel all Germans from Iran. Reza Shah refused to expel the
Germans and on 25 August 1941, the British and Soviets launched a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Soviet_invasion_of_Iran"] surprise invasion and Reza Shah's government quickly
 surrendered.[151] The invasion's strategic purpose was to secure a supply line to the USSR (later named the Persian
Corridor), secure the oil fields and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abadan_Refinery"] Abadan Refinery (of the UK-owned [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Iranian_Oil_Company"] Anglo-Iranian Oil Company), prevent a German
advance via Turkey or the USSR on Baku's oil fields, and limit German influence in Iran. Following the invasion, on 16
September 1941 Reza Shah abdicated and was replaced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi"] Mohammad Reza Pahlavi, his 21-year-old son.[152][153][154]
 During the rest of World War II, Iran became a major conduit for British and
 American aid to the Soviet Union and an avenue through which over 120,000
Polish refugees and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anders%27_Army"] Polish Armed Forces fled the Axis advance.[155] At the 1943
 Tehran Conference, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II"] Allied "Big Three"—[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin"] Joseph Stalin, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt"] Franklin D. Roosevelt,
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill"] Winston Churchill—issued the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_Conference#Three_powers_come_together"] Tehran Declaration to guarantee the post-war
independence and boundaries of Iran. However, at the end of the war, Soviet troops
remained in Iran and established two puppet states in north-western Iran, namely the
 People's Government of Azerbaijan and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Mahabad"] Republic of Mahabad. This led to the
 Iran crisis of 1946, one of the first confrontations of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War"] Cold War, which ended
after oil concessions were promised to the USSR and Soviet forces withdrew from
Iran proper in May 1946. The two puppet states were soon overthrown, and the oil
concessions were later revoked.[156][157] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II"] Allied "Big Three" at the 1943
 Tehran Conference.
1951–1978: Mosaddegh, Mohammad Reza Pahlavi
 In 1951, Mohammad Mosaddegh was appointed as the Prime Minister of Pahlavi Iran. After the nationalization of Iran's oil
industry, he became enormously popular. He was deposed in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1953 Iranian coup d'état, an Anglo-American covert
operation that marked the first time the United States had participated in an overthrow of a foreign government during the
 Cold War.[158]
After the coup, the Shah became increasingly [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocracy"] autocratic and sultanistic, and Iran entered a decades-long phase of
controversially close relations with the United States and some other foreign governments.[159] While the Shah increasingly
modernized Iran and claimed to retain it as a fully [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secular_state"] secular state,[23] arbitrary arrests and torture by his secret police, the
SAVAK, were used for crushing all forms of political opposition.[160]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany"]
Page 10
 Ruhollah Khomeini, a radical Muslim cleric,[161] became an active critic of the
Shah's far-reaching series of reforms known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Revolution"] White Revolution. Khomeini
publicly denounced the government, and was arrested and imprisoned for 18
months. After his release in 1964, he refused to apologize and was eventually sent
into exile.
Due to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_oil_crisis"] 1973 spike in oil prices, the economy of Iran was flooded with foreign
currency, which caused inflation. By 1974, the economy of Iran was experiencing a
double-digit inflation rate, and despite the many large projects to modernize the
country, corruption was rampant and caused [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Background_and_causes_of_the_Iranian_Revolution#1970%E2%80%931975"] large amounts of waste. By 1975 and
1976, an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recession"] economic recession led to an increased unemployment rate, especially
among millions of youths who had migrated to the cities of Iran looking for
construction jobs during the boom years of the early 1970s. By the late 1970s, many
of these people opposed the Shah's regime and began organizing and joining the
protests against it.[162] 
 Mohammad Reza Pahlavi and the
Imperial Family during the coronation
ceremony of the Shah of Iran in
1967.
After the 1979 Iranian Revolution
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution"] 1979 Revolution, later known as the Islamic Revolution,[163][164][165] began in
 January 1978 with the first major demonstrations against the Shah.[166] After a year of
 strikes and demonstrations paralyzing the country and its economy, Mohammad Reza
Pahlavi fled to the United States, and Ruhollah Khomeini returned from exile to Tehran in
February 1979, forming a new government.[167] After holding [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_1979_Iranian_Islamic_Republic_referendum"] a referendum, Iran officially
became an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_republic"] Islamic republic in April 1979.[168] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/December_1979_Iranian_constitutional_referendum"] A second referendum in December 1979
approved [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] a theocratic constitution.[169]
 The immediate nationwide uprisings against the new government began with the 1979
 Kurdish rebellion and the Khuzestan uprisings, along with the uprisings in Sistan and
 Baluchestan and other areas. Over the next several years, these uprisings were subdued
 violently by the new Islamic government. The new government began purging itself of the
non-Islamist political opposition, as well as of those Islamists who were not considered
radical enough. Although both nationalists and Marxists had initially joined with Islamists to 
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini%27s_return_to_Iran"] Ruhollah Khomeini's return
to Iran on 1 February 1979
overthrow the Shah, tens of thousands were executed by the new regime afterward.[170]
Following Khomeini's order to purge the new government of any remaining officials still loyal to the exiled Shah, many
former ministers and officials in the Shah's government, including former prime minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amir-Abbas_Hoveyda"] Amir-Abbas Hoveyda, were
executed.
On 4 November 1979, after the United States refusal for the extradition of Mohammad Reza Pahlavi to the new
 government, a group of Muslim students seized the United States Embassy and took the embassy with 52 personnel and
citizens hostage .[171] Attempts by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Carter"] Jimmy Carter administration to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_hostage_crisis_negotiations"] negotiate for the release of the hostages, and a failed
 rescue attempt, helped with the falling popularity of Carter among the US citizens and it pushed him out of the presidential
office and brought [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan"] Ronald Reagan to power. On Jimmy Carter's final day in office, the last hostages were finally set free
due to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algiers_Accords"] Algiers Accords. Mohammad Reza Pahlavi left the United States for Egypt, where he died of complications from
cancer only months later, on 27 July 1980.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Cultural_Revolution"] Cultural Revolution began in 1980, with an initial closure of universities for three years, in order to perform an
inspection and clean up in the cultural policy of the education and training system.[172]
On 22 September 1980, the Iraqi army [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War#1980:_Iraqi_invasion"] invaded the western Iranian province of Khuzestan, initiating the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War"] Iran–Iraq War.
Although the forces of Saddam Hussein made several early advances, by mid-1982, the Iranian forces successfully
managed to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War#1982:_Iraqi_retreat,_Iranian_offensive"] drive the Iraqi army back into Iraq. In July 1982, with Iraq thrown on the defensive, the regime of Iran decided
to invade Iraq and conducted countless offensives to conquer Iraqi territory and capture cities, such as Basra. The war
continued until 1988 when the Iraqi army defeated the Iranian forces inside Iraq and pushed the remaining Iranian troops
back across the border. Subsequently, Khomeini accepted [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_598"] a truce mediated by the United Nations. The total Iranian
 casualties in the war were estimated to be 123,220–160,000 KIA, 60,711 MIA, and 11,000–16,000 civilians
killed.[173][174]
Page 11
An Iranian soldier wearing a gas
mask on the front line during the
 Iran–Iraq War 
Following the Iran–Iraq War, in 1989,
 Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani and his
administration concentrated on a pragmatic
pro-business policy of rebuilding and
strengthening the economy without making
any dramatic break with the ideology of the
revolution. In 1997, Rafsanjani was
succeeded by moderate [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_reform_movement"] reformist
 Mohammad Khatami, whose government
attempted, unsuccessfully, to make the
country more free and democratic.[175] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Green_Movement"] Green Movement's Silent
 Demonstration during the 2009–10
Iranian election protests
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_Iranian_presidential_election"] 2005 presidential election brought
conservative [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Populist"] populist candidate, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad"] Mahmoud Ahmadinejad, to power.[176] By the
time of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Iranian_presidential_election"] 2009 Iranian presidential election, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Iran)"] Interior Ministry announced incumbent President Ahmadinejad had won
62.63% of the vote, while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mir-Hossein_Mousavi"] Mir-Hossein Mousavi had come in second place with 33.75%.[177][178] The election results were
widely disputed,[179][180] and resulted in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Iranian_presidential_election_protests"] widespread protests, both within Iran and in major cities outside the
country,[181][182] and the creation of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Green_Movement"] Iranian Green Movement.
 Hassan Rouhani was elected as the president on 15 June 2013, defeating [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Bagher_Ghalibaf"] Mohammad Bagher Ghalibaf and four other
candidates.[183][184] The electoral victory of Rouhani relatively improved the relations of Iran with other countries.[185]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Iranian_protests"] 2017–18 Iranian protests were
initiated on 31 December 2017 and
continued for months. 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Iranian_protests"] 2017–18 Iranian protests swept across the country against the government and
its longtime Supreme Leader in response to the economic and political
situation.[186] The scale of protests throughout the country and the number of
people participating were significant,[187] and it was formally confirmed that
thousands of protesters were arrested.[188] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Iranian_protests"] 2019–20 Iranian protests started on
15 November in Ahvaz, spreading across the country within hours, after the
 government announced increases in the fuel price of up to 300%.[189] A week-long
total Internet shutdown throughout the country marked one of the most severe
Internet blackouts in any country, and in the bloodiest governmental crackdown of
the protestors in the history of Islamic Republic,[190] tens of thousands were
arrested and hundreds were killed within a few days according to multiple
international observers, including [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International"] Amnesty International.[191]
On 3 January 2020, the revolutionary guard's general, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qasem_Soleimani"] Qasem Soleimani, was
 assassinated by the United States in Iraq, which considerably heightened the existing tensions between the two
countries.[192] Three days after, Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps"] Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps launched a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Iranian_attack_on_U.S._forces_in_Iraq"] retaliatory attack on US forces in Iraq
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine_International_Airlines_Flight_752_protests"] and by accident shot down Ukraine International Airlines Flight 752, killing 176 civilians and leading to nation-wide
protests. An international investigation led to the government admitting to the shootdown of the plane by a surface-to-air
missile after three days of denial, calling it a "human error".[193][194]
Geography
Iran has an area of 1,648,195 km2 (636,372 sq mi).[3] It lies between latitudes [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/24th_parallel_north"] 24°
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/40th_parallel_north"] 40° N, and longitudes [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/44th_meridian_east"] 44° and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/64th_meridian_east"] 64° E. It is bordered to the northwest by
 Armenia (35 km or 22 mi),  the Azeri exclave of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic"] Nakhchivan (179 km or
111 mi),[195] and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan"] Republic of Azerbaijan (611 km or 380 mi); to the north by the
 Caspian Sea; to the northeast by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmenistan"] Turkmenistan (992 km or 616 mi); to the east by
 Afghanistan (936 km or 582 mi) and Pakistan (909 km or 565 mi); to the south by
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf"] Persian Gulf and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman"] Gulf of Oman; and to the west by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq"] Iraq (1,458 km or
906 mi) and Turkey (499 km or 310 mi).
Iran located in seismically active area.[196] On average every 10 years one 7 Richter
earthquake occurs in Iran.[197] Most earthquakes are shallow-focus and can be very
devastating like the tragic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_Bam_earthquake"] 2003 Bam earthquake. 
 Mount Damavand, Iran's highest
point, is located in Amol,
Mazenderan.
Page 12
Iran consists of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Plateau"] Iranian Plateau, with the exception of the coasts of the Caspian Sea and Khuzestan. It is one of the
world's most mountainous countries, its landscape dominated by rugged [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_range"] mountain ranges that separate various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drainage_basin"] basins or
 plateaux from one another. The populous western part is the most mountainous, with ranges such as the Caucasus, Zagros,
and Alborz, the last containing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Damavand"] Mount Damavand, Iran's highest point at 5,610 m (18,406 ft), which is also the highest
mountain in Asia west of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush.
The northern part of Iran is covered by the lush lowland [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Hyrcanian_mixed_forests"] Caspian Hyrcanian mixed forests, located near the southern shores
of the Caspian Sea. The eastern part consists mostly of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert"] desert basins, such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dasht-e_Kavir"] Kavir Desert, which is the country's largest
desert, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dasht-e_Loot"] Lut Desert, as well as some [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_lake"] salt lakes. Iran had a 2019 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index"] Forest Landscape Integrity Index mean score of
7.67/10, ranking it 34th globally out of 172 countries.[198]The only large [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plain"] plains are found along the coast of the Caspian
Sea and at the northern end of the Persian Gulf, where the country borders the mouth of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab"] Arvand river. Smaller,
discontinuous plains are found along the remaining coast of the Persian Gulf, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz"] Strait of Hormuz, and the Gulf of Oman.
Climate
Having 11 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate"] climates out of the world's 13, Iran's climate is diverse,[199] ranging from
 arid and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-arid_climate"] semi-arid, to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subtropics"] subtropical along the Caspian coast and the northern
forests.[200] On the northern edge of the country (the Caspian coastal plain),
temperatures rarely fall below freezing and the area remains humid for the rest of the
year. Summer temperatures rarely exceed 29 °C (84.2 °F).[201][202] Annual
precipitation is 680 mm (26.8 in) in the eastern part of the plain and more than
1,700 mm (66.9 in) in the western part. Gary Lewis, the United Nations Resident
Coordinator for Iran, has said that "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_scarcity"] Water scarcity poses the most severe human
security challenge in Iran today".[203] 
Climate map of Iran ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen-Geiger"] Köppen-Geiger)
    Hot [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_desert_climate"] desert climate
    Cold [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_desert_climate"] desert climate
To the west, settlements in the Zagros basin experience lower temperatures, severe
winters with below zero average daily temperatures and heavy snowfall. The
eastern and central basins are arid, with less than 200 mm (7.9 in) of rain, and have
occasional deserts.[204] Average summer temperatures rarely exceed 38 °C 
    Hot [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate"] semi-arid climate
    Cold [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate"] semi-arid climate
    Hot-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate"] summer Mediterranean climate
    Continental [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_continental_climate"] Mediterranean climate
(100.4 °F).[201] The coastal plains of the Persian Gulf and Gulf of Oman in
southern Iran have mild winters, and very humid and hot summers. The annual precipitation ranges from 135 to 355 mm
(5.3 to 14.0 in).[201]
Despite [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_Iran"] climate change in the region, Iran is by far the largest of the few countries in the world which have not ratified the
 Paris Agreement.[205]
Wildlife
The wildlife of Iran includes bears, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_lynx"] Eurasian lynx, foxes, gazelles, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_wolf"] gray wolves,
 jackals, panthers, and wild pigs.[206][207] Domestic animals include Asian water
buffaloes, camels, cattle, donkeys, goats, horses, and sheep. Eagles, falcons,
partridges, pheasants, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stork"] storks are also native to Iran.
 One of the most famous species of animal is the critically endangered Asiatic
cheetah, also known as the Iranian cheetah, whose numbers were greatly reduced
after the 1979 Revolution.[208] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_leopard"] Persian leopard, which is the world's largest
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopard"] leopard subspecies and lives primarily in northern Iran, is also endangered.[209] Iran
lost all its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiatic_lion"] Asiatic lions and the now extinct [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_tiger"] Caspian tigers by the earlier part of the
20th century.[210] 
 Persian leopard, listed as
 Endangered on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IUCN_Red_List"] IUCN Red List.
At least 74 species of Iranian wildlife are on the red list of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature"] International Union for Conservation of Nature, a sign of
serious threats against the country's biodiversity. The Iranian Parliament has been showing disregard for wildlife by passing
laws and regulations such as the act that lets the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Industries_and_Mines_(Iran)"] Ministry of Industries and Mines exploit mines without the involvement of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_of_Environment_(Iran)"] Department of Environment, and by approving large national development projects without demanding comprehensive
study of their impact on wildlife habitats.[211]
Page 13
Administrative divisions
Iran is divided into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regions_of_Iran"] five regions with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provinces_of_Iran"] thirty-one provinces
(ostān),[212] each governed by an appointed governor
(ostāndār).  The provinces are divided into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counties_of_Iran"] counties
(šahrestān),  and subdivided into districts ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bakhsh"] baxš) and sub-
districts (dehestān).
The country has one of the highest urban growth rates in the
world. From 1950 to 2002, the urban proportion of the
population increased from 27% to 60%.[213] Most internal
migrants have settled around the cities of Tehran, Isfahan,
Ahvaz, and Qom. The listed populations are from the 2006/07
(1385 AP) census.[214]
Tehran, with a population of around 8.8 million (2016 census),
is Iran's capital and largest city. It is an economical and cultural
center, and is the hub of the country's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communications_in_Iran"] communication and
 transport network.

The country's second most populous city, Mashhad, has a
population of around 3.3 million (2016 census), and is capital of the province of
 Razavi Khorasan. Being the site of the Imam Reza Shrine, it is a holy city in Shia
Islam. About 15 to 20 million pilgrims visit the shrine every year.[215][216]
 Isfahan has a population of around 2.2 million (2016 census), and is Iran's third
most populous city. It is the capital of the province of Isfahan, and was also the third
capital of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safavid_dynasty"] Safavid Empire. It is home to a wide variety of historical sites,
including the famous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naqsh-e_Jahan_Square"] Shah Square, Siosepol, and the churches at the Armenian
district of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Julfa"] New Julfa. It is also home to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_shopping_malls"] world's seventh-largest shopping mall,
 Isfahan City Center.
The fourth most populous city of Iran, Karaj, has a population of around 1.9 million Iran's most populated cities (2010)
(2016 census). It is the capital of the province of Alborz, and is situated 20 km west
of Tehran, at the foot of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alborz"] Alborz mountain range. It is a major industrial city in Iran, with large factories producing sugar,
textiles, wire, and alcohol.
With a population of around 1.7 million (2016 census), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabriz"] Tabriz is the fifth most populous city of Iran, and had been the
second most populous until the late 1960s. It was the first capital of the Safavid Empire and is now the capital of the
province of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Azerbaijan_Province"] East Azerbaijan. It is also considered the country's second major industrial city (after Tehran).
Shiraz, with a population of around 1.8 million (2016 census), is Iran's sixth most populous city. It is the capital of the
province of Fars, and was also the capital of Iran under the reign of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zand_dynasty"] Zand dynasty. It is located near the ruins of
 Persepolis and Pasargadae, two of the four capitals of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire.

Government and politics
The political system of the Islamic Republic is based on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] 1979 Constitution.[217] 
430,871
Supreme Leader
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran"] Leader of the Revolution ("Supreme Leader") is responsible for delineation and
supervision of the policies of the Islamic Republic of Iran.[220] The Iranian
president has limited power compared to the Supreme Leader Khamenei.[221] The
current longtime Supreme Leader, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei"] Ali Khamenei, has been issuing decrees and 
Iran's syncretic political system
combines elements of an Islamic

making the final decisions on the economy, environment, foreign policy, education,
national planning, and everything else in  the

guidelines and urges for the transparency,[230] and has fired and reinstated
presidential cabinet appointments.[231][232] Key ministers are selected with the
Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei's agreement and he has the ultimate say on Iran's
foreign policy.[221] The president-elect is required to gain the Leader Khamenei's
official approval before being sworn in before the Parliament (Majlis). Through this
process, known as Tanfiz (validation), the Leader agrees to the outcome of the
presidential election. The Supreme Leader is directly involved in ministerial
appointments for Defense, Intelligence and Foreign Affairs, as well as other top
ministries after submission of candidates from the president.[233] Iran's regional
policy is directly controlled by the office of the Supreme Leader with the Ministry
of Foreign Affairs' task limited to protocol and ceremonial occasions. All of Iran's
ambassadors to Arab countries, for example, are chosen by the Quds Corps, which

The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran"] Supreme Leader is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-chief"] commander-in-chief of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] armed forces, controls the
military intelligence and security operations, and has sole power to declare war or
peace.[220] The heads of the judiciary, the state radio and television networks, the
commanders of the police and military forces, and six of the twelve members of the
 Guardian Council are directly appointed by the Supreme Leader.[220]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_of_Experts"] Assembly of Experts is responsible for electing the Supreme Leader, and has
the power to dismiss him on the basis of qualifications and popular esteem.[239] To
date, the Assembly of Experts has not challenged any of the Supreme Leader's
decisions, nor has it attempted to dismiss him.[240] The previous head of the judicial
system, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadeq_Larijani"] Sadeq Larijani, appointed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran"] Supreme Leader, said that it is illegal for
the Assembly of Experts to supervise the Supreme Leader.[241] Due to Khamenei's 
Ali Khamenei voting in the 2017
presidential election
very longtime unchallenged rule, many believe the Assembly of Experts has become a ceremonial body without any real
power.[242][243][244][245] There have been instances when the current Supreme Leader publicly criticized members of the
Assembly of Experts, resulting in their arrest and dismissal. For example, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khamenei"] Khamenei publicly called then-member of the
Assembly of Experts [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Azari_Qomi"] Ahmad Azari Qomi a traitor, resulting in Qomi's arrest and eventual dismissal from the Assembly of
Experts. Another instance is when Khamenei indirectly called [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akbar_Hashemi_Rafsanjani"] Akbar Hashemi Rafsanjani a traitor for a statement he made,
causing Rafsanjani to retract it.[246]
Guardian Council
Page 15
Presidential candidates and parliamentary candidates must be approved by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardian_Council"] Guardian Council (all members of which are
 directly or indirectly appointed by the Leader) or the Leader before running to ensure their allegiance to the Supreme
Leader.[247] The Leader very rarely does the vetting himself directly but has the power to do so, in which case additional
approval of the Guardian Council would not be needed. The Leader can also revert the decisions of the Guardian
Council.[248] The Guardian Council can, and has dismissed some elected members of the Iranian parliament in the past.[249]
For example, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minoo_Khaleghi"] Minoo Khaleghi was disqualified by Guardian Council even after winning election, as she had been
photographed in a meeting without wearing headscarf.[250]
President
After the Supreme Leader, the Constitution defines the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Iran"] President of Iran as the
highest state authority.[220][254] The President is elected by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_suffrage"] universal suffrage for a
term of four years, however, the president is still required to gain the Leader's
official approval before being sworn in before the Parliament (Majlis). The Leader
also has the power to dismiss the elected president anytime.[255] The President can
only be re-elected for one term.[254]
The President is responsible for the implementation of the constitution, and for the
exercise of executive powers in implementing the decrees and general policies as
outlined by the Supreme Leader, except for matters directly related to the Supreme
Leader, who has the final say in all matters.[220] Unlike the executive in other 
 Iranian former President Hassan
Rouhani meeting with Russian
President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin"] Vladimir Putin. Iran and
Russia are strategic
countries, the President of Iran does not have full control over anything, as these are
ultimately under the control of the Supreme Leader.[217] Chapter IX of the 
allies.[251][252][253]
 Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran sets forth the qualifications for
presidential candidates. The procedures for presidential election and all other elections in Iran are outlined by the Supreme
Leader.[230][256] The President functions as the executive of affairs such as signing treaties and other international
agreements, and administering national planning, budget, and state employment affairs, all as approved by the Supreme
Leader.[223][224][256][225][226][227][228][257]
The President appoints the ministers, subject to the approval of the Parliament, as well as the approval of the Supreme
Leader, who can dismiss or reinstate any of the ministers at any time, regardless of the decisions made by the President or
the Parliament.[231][232][258] The President supervises the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Iran"] Council of Ministers, coordinates government decisions, and
selects government policies to be placed before the legislature.[259] The current Supreme Leader, Ali Khamenei, has fired as
well as reinstated Council of Ministers members.[260][261] Eight Vice Presidents serve under the President, as well as a
cabinet of twenty-two ministers, who must all be approved by the legislature.[262]
Legislature
The legislature of Iran, known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Consultative_Assembly"] Islamic Consultative Assembly, is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicameralism"] unicameral
body comprising 290 members elected for four-year terms.[263] It drafts legislation,
ratifies international treaties, and approves the national budget. All parliamentary
candidates and all legislation from the assembly must be approved by the Guardian
Council.[264]
The Guardian Council comprises twelve jurists, including six appointed by the
Supreme Leader. Others are elected by the Parliament, from among the jurists
nominated by the Head of the Judiciary.[265][266] The Council interprets the
constitution and may veto the Parliament. If a law is deemed incompatible with the 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Consultative_Assembly"] Islamic Consultative Assembly,
also known as the Iranian Parliament
constitution or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] Sharia (Islamic law),  it is referred back to the Parliament for
revision.[254] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expediency_Discernment_Council"] Expediency Council has the authority to mediate disputes between the Parliament and the Guardian
Council, and serves as an advisory body to the Supreme Leader, making it one of the most powerful governing bodies in the
country.[267] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City_and_Village_Councils_of_Iran"] Local city councils are elected by public vote to four-year terms in all cities and villages of Iran.
Law
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_system_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"]
Page 16
The Supreme Leader appoints the head of the country's judiciary, appointing the head of the Supreme Court and the chief
public prosecutor.[240] There are several types of courts, including public courts that deal with civil and criminal cases, and
 revolutionary courts which deal with certain categories of offenses, such as crimes against [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_security"] national security. The decisions
of the revolutionary courts are final and cannot be appealed.[240]
The Chief Justice of Iran is the head of the Judicial system of the Islamic Republic of Iran and is responsible for its
administration and supervision. He is also the highest judge of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Iran"] Supreme Court of Iran. The Supreme Leader of Iran
appoints and can dismiss the Chief Justice. The Chief Justice nominates some candidates for serving as minister of justice,
and then the President select one of them. The Chief Justice can serve for two five-year terms.[268]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Clerical_Court"] Special Clerical Court handles crimes allegedly committed by clerics, although it has also taken on cases involving
laypeople. The Special Clerical Court functions independently of the regular judicial framework, and is accountable only to
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran"] Supreme Leader. The Court's rulings are final and cannot be appealed.[240] The Assembly of Experts, which meets for
one week annually, comprises 86 "virtuous and learned" clerics elected by adult suffrage for eight-year terms.
Foreign relations 
Since the time of the 1979 Revolution, Iran's foreign relations have often been
portrayed as being based on two strategic principles; eliminating outside influences
 in the region, and pursuing extensive diplomatic contacts with developing and non-
aligned countries.[269]
