Since 2005, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran"] Iran's nuclear program has become the subject of contention with the
international community, mainly the United States. Many countries have expressed
concern that Iran's nuclear program could divert civilian nuclear technology into a
 weapons program. This has led the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council"] United Nations Security Council to impose
 sanctions against Iran which had further isolated Iran politically and economically
 from the rest of the global community. In 2009, the U.S. Director of National
Intelligence said that Iran, if choosing to, would not be able to develop a nuclear
As of 2009, the government of Iran maintains diplomatic relations with 99 members
of the United Nations,[271] but not with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93United_States_relations"] United States, and not with Israel—a
state which Iran's government has derecognized since the 1979 Revolution.[272]
Among Muslim nations, Iran has an adversarial relationship with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_relations"] Saudi Arabia due
to different political and Islamic ideologies. While Iran is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia"] Shia Islamic Republic,
 Saudi Arabia is a conservative Sunni monarchy.[273] Regarding the Israeli–
Palestinian conflict, the government of Iran has recognized [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem"] Jerusalem as the capital
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_Palestine"] State of Palestine, after Trump recognized Jerusalem as the capital of
Israel.[274][275][276]

part of the basis of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran"] international sanctions against the country. On 14 July 2015,

Tehran and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P5%2B1"] P5+1 came to a historic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action"] agreement (Joint Comprehensive Plan of
Action) to end [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1929"] economic sanctions in exchange for Iran's restriction in producing
 enriched uranium after demonstrating a peaceful nuclear research project that would meet the International Atomic Energy
Agency standards.[277]
Iran is a member of dozens of international organizations, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_of_15"] G-15, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_of_24"] G-24, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_of_77"] G-77, IAEA, IBRD, IDA, IDB, IFC,

Organization (SCO), a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia"] Eurasian political, economic, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Security"] security alliance.[279][280]
Military
Page 17
The Islamic Republic of Iran has two types of armed forces: the regular forces of the
Army, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran_Air_Force"] Air Force, and the Navy, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps"] Revolutionary Guards, totaling about
545,000 active troops. Iran also has around 350,000 Reserve Force, totaling around
900,000 trained troops.[281]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps"] The government of Iran has a paramilitary, volunteer militia force within the Islamic
Revolutionary Guard Corps, called the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basij"] Basij, which includes about 90,000 full-
time, active-duty uniformed members. Up to 11 million men and women are
members of the Basij who could potentially be called up for service.
GlobalSecurity.org estimates Iran could mobilize "up to one million men", which
would be among the largest troop mobilizations in the world.[282] In 2007, Iran's
military spending represented 2.6% of the GDP or $102 per capita, the lowest figure
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf"] Persian Gulf nations.[283] Iran's military doctrine is based on deterrence.[284]
 In 2014, the country spent $15 billion on arms, while the states of the Gulf
Cooperation Council spent eight times more.[285] 
Sophisticated indigenous long range
missile system [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavar-373"] Bavar-373 paraded in
Tehran.
The government of Iran supports the military activities of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_Iran"] its allies in Syria, Iraq, and Lebanon (Hezbollah) with military and
financial aid.[286] Iran and Syria are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Syria_relations"] close strategic allies, and Iran has provided [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_involvement_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War"] significant support for the Syrian
Government in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War"] Syrian Civil War.[287] According to some estimates, Iran controlled over 80,000 pro-Assad [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shi'ite
fighters in Syria.[287][288]
Since the 1979 Revolution, to overcome foreign embargoes, the government of Iran has developed its own military industry,
produced its own tanks, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armoured_personnel_carrier"] armored personnel carriers, missiles, submarines, military vessels, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_frigate_Jamaran"] missile destroyer, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radar"] radar systems,
helicopters, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fighter_aircraft"] fighter planes.[289] In recent years, official announcements have highlighted the development of weapons
such as the Hoot, Kowsar, Zelzal, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fateh-110"] Fateh-110, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahab-3"] Shahab-3, Sejjil, and a variety of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle"] unmanned aerial vehicles (UAVs).[290] Iran
has the largest and most diverse [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_missile"] ballistic missile arsenal in the Middle East.[291] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fajr-3_(missile)"] Fajr-3, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquid_fuel"] liquid fuel missile with an
undisclosed range which was developed and produced domestically, is currently the most advanced ballistic missile of the
country.
In June 1925, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Shah"] Reza Shah introduced conscription law at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Consultative_Majlis"] National Consultative Majlis. At that time, every male person who
had reached 21 years old must serve in the military for two years. The conscription exempted women from military service
after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_revolution"] 1979 revolution. Iranian constitution obliges all men of 18 years old and higher to serve on military or police bases.
They cannot leave the country or be employed without completion of the service period.[292] The period varies from 18 to
24 months.
Human rights
According to international reports, Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] human rights record is exceptionally poor. The regime in Iran is
undemocratic,[293][294] has frequently persecuted and arrested critics of the government and its Supreme Leader, and
severely restricts the participation of candidates in popular elections as well as other forms of political activity.[295][296]
 Women's rights in Iran are described as seriously inadequate,[297] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Children%27s_rights"] children's rights have been severely violated, with
more child offenders being executed in Iran than in any other country in the world.[298][299] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Iran"] Sexual activity between
members of the same sex is illegal and is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_penalty_for_homosexuality"] punishable by up to death.[300][301]
 Over the past decade, numbers of anti-government protests have broken out throughout Iran (such as the 2019–20 Iranian
protests), demanding reforms or the end to the Islamic Republic. However, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IRGC"] IRGC and police often suppressed mass
protests violently, resulting in thousands of protesters being killed.
In January 2021, Iranian authorities added Signal to the list of blocked social media platforms, which included Facebook,
Telegram, Twitter and YouTube. They carried out arbitrary arrests for social media postings deemed "counter-revolutionary"
or "un-Islamic".[302]
Economy
 Iran's economy is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_economy"] mixture of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_economy"] central planning, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_ownership"] state ownership of oil and other large enterprises, village agriculture, and
small-scale private trading and service ventures.[303] In 2017, GDP was $427.7 billion ($1.631 trillion at PPP), or $20,000
at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity"] PPP per capita.[3] Iran is ranked as an lower-middle income economy by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank"] World Bank.[304] In the early 21st century,
Page 18
the service sector contributed the largest percentage of the GDP, followed by
industry ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mining_in_Iran"] mining and manufacturing) and agriculture.[305]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran is responsible for developing and
maintaining the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_rial"] Iranian rial, which serves as the country's currency. The
government does not recognize [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_trade_unions#Iran"] trade unions other than the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_labor_law"] Islamic labour councils,
which are subject to the approval of employers and the security services.[306] The
minimum wage in June 2013 was 487 million rials a month ($134).[307]
Unemployment has remained above 10% since 1997, and the unemployment rate
for women is almost double that of the men.[307]
In 2006, about 45% of the government's budget came from oil and natural gas
revenues, and 31% came from taxes and fees.[308] As of 2007, Iran had earned $70
billion in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign-exchange_reserves"] foreign-exchange reserves, mostly (80%) from crude oil exports.[309]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_subsidy_reform_plan"] Iranian budget deficits have been a chronic problem, mostly due to large-scale state
subsidies, that include foodstuffs and especially gasoline, totaling more than $84
 billion in 2008 for the energy sector alone.[310][311] In 2010, the economic reform
plan was approved by parliament to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_subsidy_reform_plan"] cut subsidies gradually and replace them with
targeted social assistance. The objective is to move towards [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_market"] free market prices in a
five-year period and increase productivity and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_justice"] social justice.[312] 
 Iran's provinces by their contribution
to national GDP (2014)
The administration continues to follow the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_subsidy_reform_plan"] market reform plans of the previous one,
and indicates that it will diversify Iran's oil-reliant economy. Iran has also developed
a biotechnology, nanotechnology, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmaceuticals_in_Iran"] pharmaceutical industry.[313] However,
nationalized industries such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonyad"] bonyads have often been managed badly, making
them ineffective and uncompetitive with years. Currently, the
government is trying to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privatization_in_Iran"] privatize these industries, and, despite
successes, there are still several problems to be overcome, such as the
 lagging corruption in the public sector and lack of competitiveness.

development
Iran has leading manufacturing industries in the fields of automobile
manufacture, transportation, construction materials, home appliances,
food and agricultural goods, armaments, pharmaceuticals, information
technology, and petrochemicals in the Middle East.[314] According to
the 2012 data from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization"] Food and Agriculture Organization, Iran has
 been among the world's top five producers of apricots, cherries, sour
cherries, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cucumber"] cucumbers and gherkins, dates, eggplants, figs, pistachios,
quinces, walnuts, and watermelons.[315]  A proportional representation of Iran exports, 2019
Economic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran"] sanctions against Iran, such as the embargo against Iranian
crude oil, have injured the economy.[316] In 2015, Iran and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P5%2B1"] P5+1 reached a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action"] deal on the nuclear program that removed
 the main sanctions pertaining to Iran's nuclear program by 2016.[317] According to the BBC, renewed U.S. sanctions
against Iran "have led to a sharp downturn in Iran's economy, pushing the value of its currency to record lows, quadrupling
its annual inflation rate, driving away foreign investors, and triggering protests."[318]
Tourism
Although tourism declined significantly during the war with Iraq, it has been
subsequently recovered.[320] About 1,659,000 foreign tourists visited Iran in 2004,
and 2.3 million in 2009, mostly from Asian countries, including the republics of
 Central Asia, while about 10% came from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union"] European Union and North
America.[321][322] Since the removal of some sanctions against Iran in 2015,
tourism has re-surged in the country. Over five million tourists visited Iran in the
fiscal year of 2014–2015, four percent more than the previous year.[323][324] 
 More than a million tourists visit Kish
Alongside the capital, the most popular tourist destinations are Isfahan, Mashhad,
and Shiraz.[325] In the early 2000s, the industry faced serious limitations in 
Island each year.[319]
infrastructure, communications, industry standards, and personnel training.[326] The majority of the 300,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Travel_visa"] travel visas
granted in 2003 were obtained by Asian Muslims, who presumably intended to visit [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pilgrimage"] pilgrimage sites in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashhad"] Mashhad and Qom.
Page 19
Several organized tours from Germany, France, and other European countries come to Iran annually to visit archaeological
sites and monuments. In 2003, Iran ranked 68th in tourism revenues worldwide.[327] According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO"] UNESCO and the
 deputy head of research for Iran's Tourism Organization, Iran is rated fourth among the top 10 destinations in the Middle
East.[327] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_tourism"] Domestic tourism in Iran is one of the largest in the world.[328][329][330] Weak advertising, unstable regional
conditions, a poor public image in some parts of the world, and absence of efficient planning schemes in the tourism sector
have all hindered the growth of tourism.
Transportation
Iran has a long paved road system linking most of its towns and all of its cities. In 2011 the country had 173,000 kilometers
(107,000 mi) of roads, of which 73% were paved.[331] In 2008 there were nearly 100 passenger cars for every 1,000
inhabitants.[332]
Trains operate on 11,106 km (6,942 mi) of railroad track.[333] The country's major port of entry is [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar-Abbas"] Bandar-Abbas on the
 Strait of Hormuz. After arriving in Iran, imported goods are distributed throughout the country by trucks and freight trains.
The Tehran–[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar-Abbas"] Bandar-Abbas railroad, opened in 1995, connects Bandar-Abbas to the railroad system of Central Asia via
Tehran and Mashhad. Other major ports include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar-e_Anzali"] Bandar e-Anzali and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar_Torkaman"] Bandar e-Torkeman on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea"] Caspian Sea and
 Khorramshahr and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar_Imam"] Bandar-e Emam Khomeyni on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf"] Persian Gulf.
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Iran"] Dozens of cities have airports that serve passenger and cargo planes. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_Air"] Iran Air, the national airline, was founded in 1962 and
operated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_Air_destinations"] domestic and international flights. All large cities have mass transit systems using buses, and several private
companies provide bus services between cities.
 Transport in Iran is inexpensive because of the government's subsidization of the price of gasoline. The downside is a huge
 draw on government coffers, economic inefficiency because of highly wasteful consumption patterns, smuggling to
neighboring countries and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Iran"] air pollution. In 2008, more than one million people worked in the transportation sector,
accounting for 9% of GDP.[334]
Energy
Iran has the world's second largest proved [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves_in_Iran"] gas reserves after Russia, with 33.6
trillion [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cubic_meter"] cubic meters,[336] and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_production"] third largest natural gas production after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia"] Indonesia
and Russia. It also ranks fourth in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Iran"] oil reserves with an estimated 153,600,000,000
 barrels.[337][338] It is OPEC's second largest oil exporter, and is an energy
superpower.[339]In 2005, Iran spent US$4 billion on fuel imports, because of
 contraband and inefficient domestic use.[340] Oil industry output averaged 4 million
barrels per day (640,000 m3/d) in 2005, compared with the peak of six million
barrels per day reached in 1974. In the early 2000s, industry infrastructure was
increasingly inefficient because of technological lags. Few exploratory [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_well"] wells were
drilled in 2005.
In 2004, a large share of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves_in_Iran"] Iran's natural gas reserves were untapped. The addition of
new [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydroelectricity"] hydroelectric stations and the streamlining of conventional coal and oil-fired
stations increased installed capacity to 33,000 megawatts. Of that amount, about
75% was based on natural gas, 18% on oil, and 7% on hydroelectric power. In
2004, Iran opened its first wind-powered and geothermal plants, and the first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_power"] solar
thermal plant was to come online in 2009. Iran is the world's third country to have
developed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_to_liquids"] GTL technology.[341] 
Iran holds 10% of the world's proven
 oil reserves and 15% of its gas. It is
 OPEC's second-largest exporter and
the world's 7th largest oil
producer.[335]
 Demographic trends and intensified industrialization have caused [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_power"] electric power demand to grow by 8% per year. The
 government's goal of 53,000 megawatts of installed capacity by 2010 is to be reached by bringing on line new gas-fired
plants, and adding hydropower and nuclear power generation capacity. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bushehr_Nuclear_Power_Plant"] Iran's first nuclear power plant at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bushire"] Bushire went
online in 2011. It is the second [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant"] nuclear power plant ever built in the Middle East after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metsamor_Nuclear_Power_Plant"] Metsamor Nuclear Power Plant in
Armenia.[342][343]
Education, science and technology
Page 20
 Education in Iran is highly centralized. K–12 is supervised by the Ministry of
 Education, and higher education is under the supervision of the Ministry of Science
and Technology. According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fars_News_Agency"] Fars News Agency, the adult literacy rated 93.0% in
September 2015,[344] while according to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO"] UNESCO it had rated 85.0% in 2008 (up
from 36.5% in 1976).[345]
According to the data provided by UNESCO, Iran's literacy rate among people
aged 15 years and older was 85.54% as of 2016, with men (90.35%) being
significantly more educated than women (80.79%), with the number of illiterate
people of the same age amounting to around 8,700,000 of the country's 85 million
population.[346] According to this report, Iranian government's expenditure on
education amounts to around 4% of the GDP. 
Literacy rate of Iran's population plus
15, 1975–2015, according to
UNESCO Institute of Statistics
The requirement to enter into higher education is to have a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_school_diploma"] high school diploma and
pass the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_University_Entrance_Exam"] Iranian University Entrance Exam (officially known as konkur (‎کنکور)),
 which is the equivalent of the SAT and ACT exams of the United States. Many students do a 1–2-year course of pre-
university (piš-dānešgāh), which is the equivalent of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Education"] GCE [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level"] A-levels and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Baccalaureate"] International Baccalaureate. The completion
of the pre-university course earns students the Pre-University Certificate.[347]
Iran's higher education is sanctioned by different levels of diplomas, including an
 associate degree (kārdāni; also known as fowq e diplom) delivered in two years, a
 bachelor's degree (kāršenāsi; also known as lisāns) delivered in four years, and a
 master's degree (kāršenāsi e aršad) delivered in two years, after which another
exam allows the candidate to pursue a doctoral program (PhD; known as
doktorā).[348]
 Sharif University of Technology is
one of Iran's most prestigious higher
education institutions. 
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities"] Webometrics Ranking of World Universities (as of January 2017),
Iran's top five universities include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_University_of_Medical_Sciences"] Tehran University of Medical Sciences (478th
 worldwide),  the University of Tehran (514th worldwide),  Sharif University of
Technology (605th worldwide),  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amirkabir_University_of_Technology"] Amirkabir University of Technology (726th
worldwide), and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarbiat_Modares_University"] Tarbiat Modares University (789th worldwide).[349] Iran was
ranked 60th in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index"] Global Innovation Index in 2021, up from 67th in
2020.[350][351][352]
Iran has increased its publication output nearly tenfold from 1996 through 2004, and has been ranked first in terms of output
growth rate, followed by China.[353] According to a study by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SCImago_Journal_Rank"] SCImago in 2012, Iran would rank fourth in the world in
terms of research output by 2018, if the current trend persists.[354]
In 2009, a SUSE Linux-based HPC system made by the Aerospace Research
Institute of Iran (ARI) was launched with 32 cores, and now runs 96 cores. Its
 performance was pegged at 192 GFLOPS.[355] The Iranian humanoid robot Sorena
2, which was designed by engineers at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Tehran"] University of Tehran, was unveiled in
2010. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers"] Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers (IEEE) has placed the
name of Surena among the five prominent robots of the world after analyzing its
performance.[356]
The production line for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recombinant_factor_VIIa"] AryoSeven at
the Iranian biopharmaceutical
company of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AryoGen"] AryoGen 
In the biomedical sciences, Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_Biochemistry_and_Biophysics"] Institute of Biochemistry and Biophysics has a
UNESCO chair in biology.[357] In late 2006, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_contemporary_Iranian_scientists,_scholars,_and_engineers"] Iranian scientists successfully [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloning"] cloned a
sheep by somatic cell nuclear transfer, at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royan_Institute"] Royan Research Center in Tehran.[358]
According to a study by David Morrison and Ali Khadem Hosseini (Harvard-MIT
and Cambridge), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stem_cell"] stem cell research in Iran is amongst the top 10 in the world.[359] Iran ranks 15th in the world in
nanotechnologies.[360][361][362]
Iran placed its domestically built [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite"] satellite [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omid"] Omid into orbit on the 30th anniversary of the 1979 Revolution, on 2 February
2009,[363] through its first expendable launch vehicle Safir, becoming the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country"] ninth country in the world capable of both
producing a satellite and sending it into [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space"] space from a domestically made launcher.[364]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_nuclear_program"] Iranian nuclear program was launched in the 1950s. Iran is the seventh country to produce [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uranium_hexafluoride"] uranium hexafluoride, and
controls the entire [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fuel_cycle"] nuclear fuel cycle.[365][366]
Page 21
Iranian scientists outside Iran have also made some major contributions to science.
In 1960, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Javan"] Ali Javan co-invented the first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gas_laser"] gas laser, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuzzy_set"] fuzzy set theory was
introduced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lotfi_A._Zadeh"] Lotfi A. Zadeh.[367] Iranian cardiologist [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tofy_Mussivand"] Tofigh Mussivand invented
and developed the first artificial cardiac pump, the precursor of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_heart"] artificial heart
Furthering research and treatment of diabetes, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glycated_hemoglobin"] HbA1c was discovered by
 Samuel Rahbar. A substantial number of papers in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/String_theory"] string theory are published in
 Iran.[368] Iranian American string theorist Cumrun Vafa proposed the Vafa–Witten
theorem together with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Witten"] Edward Witten. In August 2014, Iranian mathematician
 Maryam Mirzakhani became the first woman, as well as the first Iranian, to receive
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fields_Medal"] Fields Medal, the highest prize in mathematics.[369]
Demographics 
 Simorgh launch, Iranian Space
Agency
Iran is a diverse country, consisting of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnicities_in_Iran"] numerous ethnic and linguistic
groups that are unified through a shared Iranian nationality.[370]
Iran's population grew rapidly during the latter half of the 20th
century, increasing from about 19 million in 1956 to more than 84
million by July 2020.[371][372] However, Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_fertility_rate"] fertility rate has
dropped significantly in recent years, coming down from a fertility
rate of 6.5 per woman to just a little more than 2 two decades
later,[373][374] leading to a population growth rate of about 1.39% as
of 2018.[375] Due to its young population, studies project that the
growth will continue to slow until it stabilizes around 105 million by
2050.[376][377][378]
Iran hosts one of the largest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugee"] refugee populations in the world, with
almost one million refugees,[379] mostly from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_refugees"] Afghanistan and
Iraq.[380] Since 2006, Iranian officials have been working with the
 UNHCR and Afghan officials for their repatriation.[381] According
to estimates, about five million Iranian citizens have emigrated to
other countries, mostly since the 1979 Revolution.[382][383]
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] Iranian Constitution, the government is required to
provide every citizen of the country with access to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_security"] social security,
covering retirement, unemployment, old age, disability, accidents,
calamities, health and medical treatment and care services.[384] This
is covered by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxation_in_Iran"] tax revenues and income derived from public
contributions.[385]
Languages  Population of Iranian provinces and counties in 2021.
The majority of the population speaks Persian, which is also the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language"] official language of
the country. Others include speakers of several other [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_languages"] Iranian languages within the
greater [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages"] Indo-European family and languages belonging to some other ethnicities
living in Iran.
In northern Iran, mostly confined to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilan_Province"] Gilan and Mazenderan, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilaki_language"] Gilaki and
 Mazenderani languages are widely spoken, both having affinities to the neighboring
 Caucasian languages. In parts of Gilan, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talysh_language"] Talysh language is also widely spoken,
which stretches up to the neighboring [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan"] Republic of Azerbaijan. Varieties of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish_languages"] Kurdish
are widely spoken in the province of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Province"] Kurdistan and nearby areas. In Khuzestan,
 several distinct varieties of Persian are spoken. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luri_language"] Luri and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achomi_language"] Lari are also spoken in
southern Iran. 
Iran's population growth (1880–2016)
 Azerbaijani, which is by far the most spoken language in the country after Persian,[386] as well as several other Turkic
languages and dialects, is spoken in various regions of Iran, especially in the region of Azerbaijan.
Page 22
Notable minority languages in Iran include Armenian, Georgian, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Aramaic_languages"] Neo-Aramaic, and Arabic. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khuzestani_Arabic"] Khuzi Arabic is spoken by the
 Arabs in Khuzestan, as well as the wider group of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Arabs"] Iranian Arabs. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassian_languages"] Circassian was also once widely spoken by the large
Circassian minority, but, due to assimilation over the many years, no sizable number of Circassians speak the language
anymore.[387][388][389][390]
Percentages of spoken language continue to be a point of debate, as many opt that they are politically motivated; most
notably regarding the largest and second largest ethnicities in Iran, the Persians and Azerbaijanis. Percentages given by the
 CIA's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Factbook"] World Factbook include 53% Persian, 16% Azerbaijani, 10% Kurdish, 7% [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazanderani_language"] Mazenderani and Gilaki, 7% Luri, 2%
Turkmen, 2% Balochi, 2% Arabic, and 2% the remainder Armenian, Georgian, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Aramaic_languages"] Neo-Aramaic, and Circassian.[3]
Ethnic groups
As with the spoken languages, the ethnic group composition also remains a point of
debate, mainly regarding the largest and second largest ethnic groups, the Persians
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_World_Factbook"] and Azerbaijanis, due to the lack of Iranian state censuses based on ethnicity. The
CIA's World Factbook has estimated that around 79% of the population of Iran is a
diverse [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans"] Indo-European [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnolinguistics"] ethno-linguistic group that comprise speakers of various
 Iranian languages,[391] with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_people"] Persians (including [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazanderani_people"] Mazenderanis and Gilaks)
constituting 61% of the population, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds"] Kurds 10%, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lurs"] Lurs 6%, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baloch_people"] Balochs 2%. Peoples
of other ethnolinguistic groups make up the remaining 21%, with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Azerbaijanis"] Azerbaijanis
constituting 16%, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs"] Arabs 2%, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmens"] Turkmens and other [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_peoples"] Turkic tribes 2%, and others (such
as Armenians, Talysh, Georgians, Circassians, Assyrians) 1%.[3] 
Iran's provinces by population
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_of_Congress"] Library of Congress issued slightly different estimates: 65% Persians (including density (2013)
Mazenderanis, Gilaks, and the Talysh), 16% Azerbaijanis, 7% Kurds, 6% Lurs, 2%
Baloch, 1% Turkic tribal groups (incl. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qashqai_people"] Qashqai and Turkmens), and non-Iranian,
non-Turkic groups (incl. Armenians, Georgians, Assyrians, Circassians, and Arabs) less than 3%. It determined that Persian
is the first language of at least 65% of the country's population, and is the second language for most of the remaining
35%.[392]
Religion
 Twelver Shia Islam is the official [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_religion"] state religion, to which about 90% to
95%[394][395] of the population adhere. About 4% to 8% of the population
are Sunni Muslims, mainly [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Kurds"] Kurds and Baloches. The remaining 2% are non-
Muslim religious minorities, including Christians, Zoroastrians, Jews,
 Baháʼís, Mandeans, and Yarsanis.[3][396]
