around 90–95% of Iranian Muslims associate themselves with the Shia branch of Islam, the official state religion, and about
5–10% with the Sunni and Sufi branches of Islam.[403]
There are a large population of adherents of Yarsanism, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds_in_Iran"] Kurdish indigenous religion, making it the largest (unrecognized)
 minority religion in Iran. Its followers are mainly Gorani Kurds and certain groups of Lurs. They are based in Kurdistan
Province, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kermanshah_Province"] Kermanshah Province and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorestan"] Lorestan mainly.
Christianity, Judaism, Zoroastrianism, and the Sunni branch of Islam are officially recognized by the government and have
reserved seats in the Iranian Parliament.[145] Historically, early [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_religions"] Iranian religions such as the Proto-Iranic religion and the
subsequent [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism"] Zoroastrianism and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manichaeism"] Manichaeism were the dominant religions in Iran, particularly during the Median,
Achaemenid, Parthian, and Sasanian eras. This changed after the fall of the Sasanian Empire by the centuries-long
Page 23
 Islamization that followed the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia"] Muslim Conquest of Iran. Iran was predominantly Sunni until the conversion of the country
 (as well as the people of what is today the neighboring Republic of Azerbaijan) to Shia Islam by order of the Safavid
dynasty in the 16th century.[126]
 Judaism has a long history in Iran, dating back to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Babylon"] Achaemenid conquest of Babylonia. Although many left in the wake
of the establishment of the State of Israel and the 1979 Revolution, about 8,756[404] to 25,000[405] Jewish people live in
Iran. Iran has the largest Jewish population in the Middle East outside of Israel.[406]
Around 250,000 to 370,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_Iran"] Christians reside in Iran,[407][408] and Christianity is the country's largest recognized minority
religion.[409] Most are of Armenian background, as well as a sizable minority of Assyrians.[410] A large number of Iranians
have converted to Christianity from the predominant [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam"] Shia Islam.[411][412][413][414]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur_on_Human_Rights_in_Iran"] The Baháʼí Faith is not officially recognized and has been subject to official persecution.[415] According to the United
Nations Special Rapporteur on Human Rights in Iran, Baháʼís are the largest non-Muslim religious minority in Iran, with an
estimated 350,000 adherents.[416] Since the 1979 Revolution, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%ADs"] persecution of Baháʼís has increased with executions and
denial of civil rights, especially the denial of access to higher education and employment.[415][417][418]
Iranian officials have continued to support the rebuilding and renovation of Armenian churches in the Islamic Republic. The
 Armenian Monastic Ensembles of Iran has also received continued support. In 2019, the Iranian government registered the
 Holy Savior Cathedral, commonly referred to as Vank Cathedral, in the New Julfa district of Isfahan, as a UNESCO World
Heritage Site, with significant expenditures for its congregation. Currently three Armenian churches in Iran have been
included in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_List"] UNESCO World Heritage List.[419][420]
Culture
The earliest attested cultures in Iran date back to the Lower Paleolithic. Owing to its geopolitical position, Iran has
influenced cultures as far as Greece and Italy to the west, Russia to the north, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula"] Arabian Peninsula to the south, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] south
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Asia"] east Asia to the east.
Art
The art of Iran encompasses many disciplines, including architecture, stonemasonry,
metalworking, weaving, pottery, painting, and calligraphy. Iranian works of art
show a great variety in style, in different regions and periods.[421] The art of the
 Medes remains obscure, but has been theoretically attributed to the Scythian
style.[422] The Achaemenids borrowed heavily from the art of their neighboring
 civilizations,[423] but produced a synthesis of a unique style,[424] with an eclectic
architecture remaining at sites such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persepolis"] Persepolis and Pasargadae. Greek
iconography was imported by the Seleucids, followed by the recombination of
 Hellenistic and earlier Near Eastern elements in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_art"] art of the Parthians,[425] with
remains such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_of_Anahita,_Kangavar"] Temple of Anahita and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statue,_National_Museum_of_Iran_2401"] Statue of the Parthian Nobleman. By
the time of the Sasanians, Iranian art came across a general renaissance.[426]
Although of unclear development,[427] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_art"] Sasanian art was highly influential, and
spread into far regions. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taq_Bostan"] Taq-e-Bostan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taq_Kasra"] Taq-e-Kasra, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naqsh-e_Rustam"] Naqsh-e-Rostam, and the
 Shapur-Khwast Castle are among the surviving monuments from the Sasanian
period. 
 Iron Age gold cup from Marlik, kept
 at New York City's Metropolitan
Museum of Art
During the Middle Ages, Sasanian art played a prominent role in the formation of both European and Asian medieval
art,[91] which carried forward to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_world"] Islamic world, and much of what later became known as Islamic learning—including
medicine, architecture, philosophy, philology, and literature—were of Sasanian basis.[428][429][430][431]
The Safavid era is known as the Golden Age of Iranian art,[432] and Safavid works of art show a far more unitary
 development than in any other period,[433] as part of a political evolution that reunified Iran as a cultural entity.[433] Safavid
art exerted noticeable influences upon the neighboring Ottomans, the Mughals, and the Deccans, and was also influential
through its fashion and garden architecture on 11th–17th-century Europe.[433]
Page 24
Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_modern_and_contemporary_art"] contemporary art traces its origins back to the time of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamal-ol-molk"] Kamal-ol-Molk,[435] a
prominent [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Realism_(arts)"] realist painter at the court of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty"] Qajar dynasty who affected the norms of
painting and adopted a naturalistic style that would compete with photographic
works. A new Iranian school of fine art was established by Kamal-ol-Molk in
1928,[435] and was followed by the so-called "coffeehouse" style of painting.
Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avant-garde"] avant-garde modernists emerged by the arrival of new western influences
during World War II.[435] The vibrant contemporary art scene originates in the late
1940s, and Tehran's first modern art gallery, Apadana, was opened in September
1949 by painters Mahmud Javadipur, Hosein Kazemi, and Hushang
Ajudani.[436][437] The new movements received official encouragement by the mid-
1950s,[435] which led to the emergence of artists such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcos_Grigorian"] Marcos Grigorian,
signaling a commitment to the creation of a form of modern art grounded in
Iran.[438] 
 Kamal-ol-Molk's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirror_Hall"] Mirror Hall, often
 considered a starting point in Iranian
modern art[434]
Architecture
The history of architecture in Iran goes back to the seventh millennium BC.[439]
Iranians were among the first to use mathematics, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometry"] geometry and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomy"] astronomy in
architecture. Iranian architecture displays great variety, both structural and aesthetic,
developing gradually and coherently out of earlier traditions and experience.[440]
The guiding [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motif_(visual_arts)"] motif of Iranian architecture is its cosmic symbolism, "by which man is
brought into communication and participation with the powers of heaven".[441]
Iran ranks seventh among [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO"] UNESCO's list of countries with the most archaeological
ruins and attractions from antiquity.[442]
Traditionally, the guiding formative motif of Iranian architecture has been its cosmic
 symbolism "by which man is brought into communication and participation with
the powers of heaven".[443] This theme has not only given unity and continuity to
the architecture of Persia but has been a primary source of its emotional character as
well.
According to Persian historian and archaeologist [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Upham_Pope"] Arthur Pope, the supreme Iranian
art, in the proper meaning of the word, has always been its architecture. The
supremacy of architecture applies to both pre- and post-Islamic periods.[444] 
Ruins of the Tachara, part of the
 World Heritage Site of Persepolis.
Weaving
Iran's carpet-weaving has its origins in the Bronze Age and is one of the most
distinguished manifestations of Iranian art. Iran is the world's largest producer and
exporter of handmade carpets, producing three-quarters of the world's total output
and having a share of 30% of world's export markets.[445][446] 
 Isfahan's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Heritage_Site"] World Heritage Site of
 Naqsh-e Jahan Square.
Literature
Iran's oldest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature"] literary tradition is that of Avestan, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Iranian"] Old Iranian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacred_language"] sacred language of the Avesta, which consists of the
legendary and religious texts of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism"] Zoroastrianism and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Iranian_religion"] ancient Iranian religion, with its earliest records dating back to the
pre-Achaemenid times.[447]
Of the various modern languages used in Iran, Persian, various dialects of which are spoken throughout the Iranian
Plateau,[448][449] has the most influential literature. Persian has been dubbed as a worthy language to serve as a conduit for
poetry, and is considered one of the four main bodies of world literature.[450] Despite originating from the region of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persis"] Persis
 (better known as Persia) in southwestern Iran, the Persian language was used and developed further through Persianate
societies in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia"] Asia Minor, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia, leaving massive influences on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_poetry"] Ottoman and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language_in_the_Indian_subcontinent"] Mughal literatures,
among others.
Page 25
Iran has a number of famous medieval poets, most notably Rumi, Ferdowsi, Hafez,
 Sa'adi, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omar_Khayyam"] Omar Khayyam, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi"] Nezami Ganjavi.[451] Iranian literature also inspired
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson"] writers such as Johann Wolfgang von Goethe, Henry David Thoreau, and Ralph
Waldo Emerson.[108][109][110]
Philosophy
Zoroaster, the founder of
Zoroastrianism, depicted on
 Raphael's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_School_of_Athens"] The School of Athens 
 Iranian philosophy originates from Indo-
European roots, with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroaster"] Zoroaster's reforms
having major influences. 
Tomb of the 10th-century Persian
poet Ferdowsi, author of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahnameh"] Šāhnāme,
 According to The Oxford Dictionary of
Philosophy, the chronology of the subject 
the classical Persian composition of
the Iranian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_epic"] national epics, in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tus,_Iran"] Tus
and science of philosophy starts with the
Indo-Iranians, dating this event to 1500 BC. The Oxford dictionary also states,
"Zarathushtra's philosophy entered to influence Western tradition through Judaism,
and therefore on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Platonism"] Middle Platonism."
While there are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-Iranian_religion"] ancient relations between the Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedas"] Vedas and the Iranian Avesta,
the two main families of the Indo-Iranian philosophical traditions were characterized by fundamental differences, especially
in their implications for the human being's position in society and their view of man's role in the universe.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrus_Cylinder"] Cyrus Cylinder, which is known as "the first charter of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights"] human rights", is often seen as a reflection of the questions and
thoughts expressed by Zoroaster, and developed in Zoroastrian schools of the Achaemenid era.[452][453] The earliest tenets
of Zoroastrian schools are part of the extant scriptures of the Zoroastrian religion in Avestan. Among them are treatises such
as the Zatspram, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shikand-gumanig_Vizar"] Shkand-gumanik Vizar, and Denkard, as well as older passages of the Avesta and the Gathas.[454]
The current trends in Iranian philosophy have grown limited in scope because of Islamic frames of thought [455] although
the liberal ways of thought remain open to be generated in Iranian publications by Iranian intellectuals, especially outside
Iran, where the Iranian regime has less power to restrict Iranian thought and philosophy.
Mythology
 Iranian mythology consists of ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_folklore"] Iranian folklore and stories, all involving extraordinary beings, reflecting attitudes
towards the confrontation of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_and_evil"] good and evil, actions of the gods, and the exploits of heroes and fabulous creatures.
Myths play a crucial part in Iranian culture, and understanding of them is increased when they are considered within the
context of actual events in Iranian history. The geography of Greater Iran, a vast area covering present-day Iran, the
Caucasus, Anatolia, Mesopotamia and Central Asia, with its high mountain ranges, plays the main role in much of Iranian
mythology.
Tenth-century Persian poet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdowsi"] Ferdowsi's long [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic_poetry"] epic poem [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahnameh"] Šāhnāme ("Book of Kings"), which is for the most part based on
Xwadāynāmag, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Persian"] Middle Persian compilation of the history of Iranian kings and heroes from mythical times down to the
reign of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khosrow_II"] Chosroes II,[456] is considered the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_epic"] national epic of Iran. It draws heavily on the stories and characters of the
Zoroastrian tradition, from the texts of the Avesta, the Denkard, and the Bundahishn.
Music
Iran is the apparent birthplace of the earliest complex instruments, dating back to the third millennium BC.[457] The use of
both vertical and horizontal angular [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harp"] harps have been documented at the sites Madaktu and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kul-e_Farah"] Kul-e Farah, with the largest
collection of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elam"] Elamite instruments documented at Kul-e Farah. Multiple depictions of horizontal harps were also sculpted in
Assyrian palaces, dating back between 865 and 650 BC.
 Xenophon's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyropaedia"] Cyropaedia mentions a great number of singing women at the court of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire"] Achaemenid Empire. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athenaeus"] Athenaeus of
Naucratis, in his [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deipnosophistae"] Deipnosophistae, points out to the capture of Achaemenid singing girls at the court of the last Achaemenid
king [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_III"] Darius III (336–330 BC) by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)"] Macedonian general Parmenion. Under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire"] Parthian Empire, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gusans"] gōsān ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_language"] Parthian for
Page 26
"minstrel") had a prominent role in the society.[458] According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutarch"] Plutarch's Life of
Crassus (32.3), they praised their national heroes and ridiculed their Roman rivals.
Likewise, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strabo"] Strabo's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geographica"] Geographica reports that the Parthian youth were taught songs
about "the deeds both of the gods and of the noblest men".[459]
The history of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_music"] Sasanian music is better documented than the earlier periods and is
especially more evident in Avestan texts.[460] By the time of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khosrow_II"] Chosroes II, the
Sasanian royal court hosted a number of prominent musicians, namely Azad,
Bamshad, Barbad, Nagisa, Ramtin, and Sarkash.
Iranian traditional musical instruments include string instruments such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chang_(instrument)"] chang
(harp), qanun, santur, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rud"] rud (oud, barbat), tar, dotar, setar, tanbur, and kamanche,
wind instruments such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorna"] sorna (zurna, karna) and ney, and percussion instruments
such as tompak, kus, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daf"] daf (dayere), and naqare. 
Karna, an ancient Iranian musical
instrument from the 6th century BC,
kept at the Persepolis Museum
Iran's first symphony orchestra, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_Symphony_Orchestra"] Tehran Symphony Orchestra, was founded by Qolam-Hoseyn Minbashian in 1933. It
was reformed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parviz_Mahmoud"] Parviz Mahmoud in 1946, and is currently Iran's oldest and largest symphony orchestra. Later, by the late
1940s, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khaleqi"] Ruhollah Khaleqi founded the country's first national music society, and established the School of National Music in
1949.[461]
 Iranian pop music has its origins in the Qajar era.[462] It was significantly developed since the 1950s, using indigenous
instruments and forms accompanied by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_guitar"] electric guitar and other imported characteristics. The emergence of genres such as
 rock in the 1960s and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_hip_hop"] hip hop in the 2000s also resulted in major movements and influences in Iranian
music.[463][464][465][466]
Theater
The earliest recorded representations of dancing figures within Iran were found in
prehistoric sites such as Tepe Sialk and Tepe Mūsīān.[467] The oldest Iranian
initiation of theater and the phenomena of acting can be traced in the ancient epic
ceremonial theaters such as Sug-e Siāvuš ("mourning of Siāvaš"), as well as dances
and theater narrations of Iranian mythological tales reported by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herodotus"] Herodotus and
Xenophon.
Iran's traditional theatrical genres include Baqqāl-bāzi ("grocer play", a form of
slapstick comedy), Ruhowzi (or Taxt-howzi, comedy performed over a courtyard
pool covered with boards), Siāh-bāzi (in which the central comedian appears in
blackface), Sāye-bāzi ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shadow_play"] shadow play), Xeyme-šab-bāzi (marionette), and Arusak-
bāzi (puppetry), and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ta%27zieh"] Ta'zie (religious tragedy plays).[468] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roudaki_Hall"] Roudaki Hall, constructed
between 1957 and 1967 in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran"] Tehran
Before the 1979 Revolution, the Iranian national stage had become a famous performing scene for known international
artists and troupes,[469] with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roudaki_Hall"] Roudaki Hall of Tehran constructed to function as the national stage for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opera"] opera and ballet.
Opened on 26 October 1967, the hall is home to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_Symphony_Orchestra"] Tehran Symphony Orchestra, the Tehran Opera Orchestra, and the
 Iranian National Ballet Company, and was officially renamed Vahdat Hall after the 1979 Revolution.
 Loris Tjeknavorian's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rostam_and_Sohrab_(opera)"] Rostam and Sohrab,  based on the tragedy of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rostam_and_Sohrab"] Rostam and Sohrab from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferdowsi"] Ferdowsi's epic poem
 Šāhnāme, is an example of opera with Persian libretto. Tjeknavorian, a celebrated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Armenians"] Iranian Armenian composer and
 conductor, composed it in 25 years, and it was finally performed for the first time at Tehran's Roudaki Hall, with Darya
Dadvar in the role of Tahmina.
Cinema and animation
A third-millennium BC earthen goblet discovered at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahr-e_Sukhteh"] Burnt City, a Bronze Age urban settlement in southeastern Iran,
depicts what could possibly be the world's oldest example of animation. The artifact, associated with Jiroft, bears five
sequential images depicting a wild goat jumping up to eat the leaves of a tree.[471][472] The earliest attested Iranian
examples of visual representations, however, are traced back to the bas-reliefs of Persepolis, the ritual center of the
 Achaemenid Empire. The figures at Persepolis remain bound by the rules of grammar and syntax of visual language.[473]
The Iranian visual arts reached a pinnacle by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire"] Sasanian era, and several works from this period have been found to
Page 27
articulate movements and actions in a highly sophisticated manner. It is even
possible to see a progenitor of the cinematic close-up shot in one of these works of
art, which shows a wounded wild pig escaping from the hunting ground.[474] 
Reproduction of the 3rd-millennium
By the early 20th century, the five-year-old industry of cinema came to Iran. The
first Iranian filmmaker was probably [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirza_Ebrahim_Khan_Akkas_Bashi"] Mirza Ebrahim (Akkas Bashi),  the court
photographer of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozaffar_ad-Din_Shah_Qajar"] Mozaffar-ed-Din Shah of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty"] Qajar dynasty. Mirza Ebrahim 
BC goblet from southeastern Iran,
possibly the world's oldest example
of animation.[470]
 obtained a camera and filmed the Qajar ruler's visit to Europe. Later in 1904, Mirza
Ebrahim (Sahhaf Bashi), a businessman, opened the first public movie theater in
Tehran.[475] After him, several others like Russi Khan, Ardeshir Khan, and Ali Vakili tried
to establish new movie theaters in Tehran. Until the early 1930s, there were around 15
 cinema theaters in Tehran and 11 in other provinces.[474] The first Iranian feature film, Abi
and Rabi, was a silent comedy directed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovanes_Ohanian"] Ovanes Ohanian in 1930. The first sounded one,
 Lor Girl, was produced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardeshir_Irani"] Ardeshir Irani and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdolhossein_Sepanta"] Abd-ol-Hosein Sepanta in 1932.
Iran's animation industry began by the 1950s, and was followed by the establishment of the
influential [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_the_Intellectual_Development_of_Children_and_Young_Adults"] Institute for the Intellectual Development of Children and Young Adults in
January 1965.[476][477] The 1960s was a significant decade for Iranian cinema, with 25
commercial films produced annually on average throughout the early 60s, increasing to 65 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_Kiarostami"] Abbas Kiarostami (1940–
by the end of the decade. The majority of the production focused on melodrama and 2016), an acclaimed Iranian
thrillers. With the screening of the films [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qeysar_(film)"] Qeysar and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Cow_(1969_film)"] The Cow, directed by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masoud_Kimiai"] Masoud Kimiai film director
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dariush_Mehrjui"] Dariush Mehrjui respectively in 1969, alternative films set out to establish their status in
 the film industry and Bahram Beyzai's Downpour and Nasser Taghvai's Tranquility in the
Presence of Others followed soon. Attempts to organize a film festival, which had begun in 1954 within the framework of
the Golrizan Festival, resulted in the festival of Sepas in 1969. The endeavors also resulted in the formation of the Tehran's
World Film Festival in 1973.[478]
After the Revolution of 1979, and following the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Cultural_Revolution"] Cultural Revolution, a new age emerged in
Iranian cinema, starting with Long Live! by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khosrow_Sinai"] Khosrow Sinai and followed by many other
directors, such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_Kiarostami"] Abbas Kiarostami and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jafar_Panahi"] Jafar Panahi. Kiarostami, an acclaimed Iranian
director, planted Iran firmly on the map of world cinema when he won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palme_d%27Or"] Palme d'Or for
 Taste of Cherry in 1997.[479] The continuous presence of Iranian films in prestigious
international festivals, such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival"] Cannes Film Festival, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival"] Venice Film Festival, and the
 Berlin International Film Festival, attracted world attention to Iranian masterpieces.[480] In
2006, six Iranian films, of six different styles, represented Iranian cinema at the Berlin
International Film Festival. Critics considered this a remarkable event in the history of
Iranian cinema.[481][482]
 Asghar Farhadi, a well-known Iranian director, has received a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award"] Golden Globe Award and
two [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award"] Academy Awards, representing Iran for Best Foreign Language Film in 2012 and
2017. In 2012, he was named as one of the 100 Most Influential People in the world by the
American news magazine [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_(magazine)"] Time.
Observances 
 Behrouz Vossoughi, a well-
known Iranian actor who has
appeared in more than 90
films
Iran's official [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Year"] New Year begins with Nowruz, an ancient Iranian tradition celebrated
annually on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equinox"] vernal equinox. It is enjoyed by people adhering to different
religions, but is considered a holiday for the Zoroastrians. It was registered on the
 UNESCO's list of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity"] Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity in
2009,[483] described as the Persian New Year,[484][485][486][487] shared with a
number of other countries in which it has historically been celebrated.
On the eve of the last Wednesday of the preceding year, as a prelude to Nowruz, the
ancient festival of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaharshanbe_Suri"] Čāršanbe Suri celebrates [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atar"] Ātar ("fire") by performing rituals such
as jumping over [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonfire"] bonfires and lighting off [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firecracker"] firecrackers and fireworks.[488][489] The
Nowruz celebrations last by the end of the 13th day of the Iranian year ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farvardin"] Farvardin
13, usually coincided with 1 or 2 April), celebrating the festival of Sizdebedar,
during which the people traditionally go outdoors to picnic. 
 Haft-Seen, a customary of Nowruz,
the Iranian New Year
Page 28
Yaldā, another nationally celebrated ancient tradition,[490] commemorates the ancient goddess [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithra"] Mithra and marks the longest
night of the year on the eve of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winter_solstice"] winter solstice (čelle ye zemestān; usually falling on 20 or 21 December),[491][492] during
which families gather together to recite poetry and eat fruits—particularly the red fruits watermelon and pomegranate, as
well as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_nuts"] mixed nuts.[493][494] In some regions of the provinces of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazandaran_Province"] Mazanderan and Markazi,[495][496][497][498] there is also
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summer_solstice"] midsummer festival of Tirgān,[499] which is observed on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tir_(month)"] Tir 13 (2 or 3 July) as a celebration of water.[500][501]
Alongside the ancient Iranian celebrations, Islamic annual events such as Ramezān, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr"] Eid e Fetr, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashura"] Ruz e Āšurā are marked
by the country's large Muslim population, Christian traditions such as Noel,[502] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lent"] Čelle ye Ruze, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easter"] Eid e Pāk[503] are
observed by the Christian communities, Jewish traditions such as Purim,[504] Hanukā,[505] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passover"] Eid e Fatir (Pesah)[506][507]
are observed by the Jewish communities, and Zoroastrian traditions such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadeh"] Sade[508] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehregan"] Mehrgān are observed by the
Zoroastrians.
Public holidays
Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_calendar"] official calendar is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_Hijri_calendar"] Solar Hejri calendar, beginning at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_equinox"] vernal equinox in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere"] Northern Hemisphere, which was
first enacted by the Iranian Parliament on 31 March 1925.[509] Each of the 12 months of the Solar Hejri calendar
correspond with a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrological_sign"] zodiac sign, and the length of each year is absolutely solar.[509] The months are named after the ancient
Iranian months,[509] namely [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farvardin"] Farvardin ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fravashi"] Fravaši), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ordibehesht"] Ordibehešt ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asha"] Aša Vahišta), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khordad"] Xordād ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haurvatat"] Haurvatāt), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tir_(month)"] Tir ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tishtrya"] Tištrya), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mordad"] Amordād
([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ameretat"] Amərətāt), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahrivar"] Šahrivar ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kshatra_Vairya"] Xšaθra Vairya), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehr_(month)"] Mehr ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mithra"] Miθra), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aban_(month)"] Ābān ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aban"] Āpō), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azar"] Āzar ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atar"] Ātar), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dey_(month)"] Dey ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahura_Mazda"] Daθuš), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahman"] Bahman ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vohu_Manah"] Vohu Manah), and
 Esfand ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spenta_Armaiti"] Spəntā Ārmaiti).
Alternatively, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Lunar Hejri calendar is used to indicate Islamic events, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gregorian_calendar"] Gregorian calendar remarks the
international events.
Legal public holidays based on the Iranian solar calendar include the cultural celebrations of Nowruz ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farvardin"] Farvardin 1–4; 21–24
March) and Sizdebedar ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farvardin"] Farvardin 13; 2 April), and the political events of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Islamic_Republic_Day"] Islamic Republic Day ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farvardin"] Farvardin 12; 1 April), the
death of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini"] Ruhollah Khomeini ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khordad"] Khordad 14; 4 June), the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/5_June_1963,_demonstrations_in_Iran"] Khordad 15 event ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khordad"] Khordad 15; 5 June), the anniversary of the
 1979 Revolution ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahman"] Bahman 22; 10 February), and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalization_of_the_Iranian_oil_industry"] Oil Nationalization Day ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Esfand"] Esfand 29; 19 March).[510]
Lunar Islamic public holidays include Tasua ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Muharram 9; 30 September), Ashura ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Muharram 10; 1 October), Arba'een
([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Safar 20; 10 November), the death of Muhammad ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Safar 28; 17 November), the death of Ali al-Ridha ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Safar 29 or 30; 18
November), the birthday of Muhammad ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Rabi-al-Awwal 17; 6 December), the death of Fatimah ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Jumada-al-Thani 3;
2 March), the birthday of Ali ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Rajab 13; 10 April), Muhammad's first revelation ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Rajab 27; 24 April), the birthday of
Muhammad al-Mahdi ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Sha'ban 15; 12 May), the death of Ali ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Ramadan 21; 16 June), Eid al-Fitr ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Shawwal 1–2; 26–27
June), the death of Ja'far al-Sadiq ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Shawwal 25; 20 July), Eid al-Qurban ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Zulhijja 10; 1 September), and Eid al-Qadir
([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_calendar"] Zulhijja 18; 9 September).[510]
Cuisine
Due to its variety of ethnic groups and the influences from the neighboring cultures,
the cuisine of Iran is diverse. Herbs, along with fruits such as plums, pomegranate,
quince, prunes, apricots, and raisins, are frequently used. To achieve a balanced taste,
characteristic flavorings such as saffron, dried lime, cinnamon, and parsley are mixed
delicately and used in some special dishes. Onion and garlic are commonly used in
the preparation of the accompanying course, but are also served separately during
meals, either in raw or pickled form.
Iranian cuisine includes a wide range of main dishes, including various types of
kebab, pilaf, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stew"] stew (khoresh), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soup"] soup and āsh, and omelette. Lunch and dinner meals are
commonly accompanied by side dishes such as plain [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yogurt"] yogurt or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tzatziki"] mast-o-khiar, sabzi,
 salad Shirazi, and torshi, and might follow dishes such as borani, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirza_Ghassemi"] Mirza Qasemi, or
 kashk e bademjan as the appetizer. 
 Chelow kabab (rice and kebab), one
 of Iran's national
dishes[511][512][513]
In Iranian culture, tea (čāy) is widely consumed.[514][515] Iran is the world's seventh major tea producer,[516] and a cup of
tea is typically the first thing offered to a guest.[517] One of Iran's most popular desserts is the falude,[518] consisting of
 vermicelli in a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rose_water"] rose water syrup, which has its roots in the fourth century BC.[519][520] There is also the popular saffron ice
cream, known as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bastani_Sonnati"] bastani sonnati ("traditional ice cream"),[521] which is sometimes accompanied with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carrot_juice"] carrot juice.[522] Iran
is also famous for its caviar.[523]
Page 29
Sports
Iran is most likely the birthplace of polo,[524][525] locally known as čowgān, with its
earliest records attributed to the ancient Medes.[526] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling"] Freestyle wrestling is
traditionally considered the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_sport"] national sport of Iran, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_national_freestyle_wrestling_athletes"] national wrestlers have
 been world champions on many occasions. Iran's traditional wrestling, called košti e
 pahlevāni ("heroic wrestling"),  is registered on UNESCO's Intangible Cultural
Heritage list.
 Being a mountainous country, Iran is a venue for skiing, snowboarding, hiking, rock
climbing,[527] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountaineering"] mountain climbing.[528][529] It is home to several ski resorts, the
most famous being Tochal, Dizin, and Shemshak, all within one to three hours
traveling from the capital city Tehran.[530] The resort of Tochal, located in the
 Alborz mountain rage, is the world's fifth-highest ski resort (3,730 m or 12,238 ft at
its highest station).
Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee_of_the_Islamic_Republic_of_Iran"] National Olympic Committee was founded in 1947. Wrestlers and
 weightlifters have achieved the country's highest [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_at_the_Olympics"] records at the Olympics. In
 September 1974, Iran became the first country in West Asia to host the Asian
Games. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azadi_Sport_Complex"] Azadi Sport Complex, the largest sports complex in Iran, was originally
built for this occasion. 
An Iranian tea (čāy) tray served near
 Garden of Mausoleum of Omar
Khayyam in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nishapur"] Nishapur
 The Azadi Stadium in Tehran is West
Asia's largest football stadium.
(as of July 2017). 
 Football has been regarded as the most
 popular sport in Iran, with the men's national
team having won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup"] Asian Cup on three
occasions. The men's national team has
maintained its position as Asia's best team,
ranking 1st in Asia and 22nd in the world
according to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings"] FIFA World Rankings (as
of September 2021).[531] 
Skiers at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dizin"] Dizin Ski Resort
Volleyball is the second most popular sport in Iran.[532][533] Having won the 2011
and 2013 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asian_Men%27s_Volleyball_Championship"] Asian Men's Volleyball Championships, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_men%27s_national_volleyball_team"] men's national team is
currently the strongest team in Asia, and ranks eighth in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIVB_World_Rankings"] FIVB World Rankings
Kabaddi is one of the most popular sports played in Iran as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_national_kabaddi_team"] Iran national kabaddi team are considered as one of the
 toughest and best team in Kabaddi having produced the greatest players namely Fazel Atrachali, Meraj Sheykh, Abolfazl
 Maghsoudlou, Abozar Mohajer Mighani, Mohammad Esmaeil Nabibakhsh, Hadi Oshtorak, Hadi Tajik, Mohsen
Maghsoudlou and many more international stars.
 Basketball is also popular,[534] with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_national_basketball_team"] men's national team having won three [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIBA_Asia_Championship"] Asian Championships since 2007.
In 2016, Iran made global headlines for international female champions boycotting tournaments in Iran in chess (U.S.
Woman Grandmaster [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naz%C3%AD_Paikidze"] Nazí Paikidze)[535][536] and in shooting (Indian world champion [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heena_Sidhu"] Heena Sidhu),[537] as they refused
to enter a country where they would be forced to wear a hijab.
Media
 Iran is one of the countries with the worst freedom of the press situation, ranking 174th out of 180 countries on the Press
Freedom Index (as of 2021).[538][539] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_and_Islamic_Guidance"] Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is Iran's main government department
responsible for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_policy"] cultural policy, including activities regarding communications and information.[540]
Iran's first newspapers were published during the reign of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naser_al-Din_Shah_Qajar"] Naser al-Din Shah of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty"] Qajar dynasty in the mid-19th
century.[541] Most of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Iran"] newspapers published in Iran are in Persian, the country's official language. The country's most
widely circulated periodicals are based in Tehran, among which are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etemad"] Etemad, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ettela%27at"] Ettela'at, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kayhan"] Kayhan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamshahri"] Hamshahri, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resalat_(newspaper)"] Resalat, and
 Shargh.[329] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_Times"] Tehran Times, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_(newspaper)"] Iran Daily, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Tribune"] Financial Tribune are among English-language newspapers based in Iran.
Page 30
Television was introduced in Iran in 1958.[542] Although the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_Asian_Games"] 1974 Asian Games were broadcast in color, full color
 programming began in 1978.[542] Since the 1979 Revolution, Iran's largest media corporation is the Islamic Republic of
Iran Broadcasting (IRIB).[329] Despite the restrictions on non-domestic television, about 65% of the residents of the capital
 city and about 30 to 40% of the residents outside the capital city access worldwide television channels through satellite
dishes, although observers state that the figures are likely to be higher.[543][544]
Iran received access to the Internet in 1993. According to Internet World Stats, as of 2017, around 69.1% of the population
of Iran are Internet users.[545] Iran ranks 17th among [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_Internet_users"] countries by number of Internet users. According to the statistics
provided by the web information company of Alexa, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Search"] Google Search is Iran's most widely used search engine and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instagram"] Instagram
is the most popular online [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_networking_service"] social networking service.[546] Direct access to many worldwide mainstream websites has been
blocked in Iran, including Facebook, which has been blocked since 2009 due to the organization of anti-governmental
protests on the website.[547] However, as of 2017, Facebook has around 40 million subscribers based in Iran (48.8% of the
population) who use [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_private_network"] virtual private networks and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_server"] proxy servers to access the website.[545] Some of the officials themselves
have verified accounts on the social networking websites that are blocked by the authorities, including Facebook and
Twitter.[548] About 90% of Iran's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E-commerce"] e-commerce takes place on the Iranian online store of Digikala, which has around
 750,000 visitors per day and more than 2.3 million subscribers and is the most visited online store in the Middle
East.[549][546]
Fashion and clothing
 Fashion in Iran is divided into several historical periods. The exact date of the emergence of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weaving"] weaving in Iran is not yet
known, but it is likely to coincide with the emergence of civilization. Clothing in Iran is mentioned in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_mythology"] Persian mythology.
 Ferdowsi and many historians have considered [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keyumars"] Keyumars to be the inventor of the use of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_skin"] animals' skin and hair as clothing.
Some historians have also mentioned [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hushang"] Hushang as the first inventor of the use of living skins as clothing.[550] Ferdowsi
considers [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahmuras"] Tahmuras to be a kind of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Textile"] textile initiator in Iran. There are historical discoveries in northern Iran from about 6,000
BC that refer to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wool"] wool weaving at the time. Other discoveries in central Iran dating back to 4200 BC have shown that the
animals' skin has not been the only clothing worn on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Plateau"] Iranian Plateau since those years. The clothing of ancient Iran took
an advanced form, and the fabric and color of clothing became very important at that time. Depending on the social status,
eminence, climate of the region and the season, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_clothing"] Persian clothing during the Achaemenian period took various forms. The
philosophy used in this clothing, in addition to being functional, also had an aesthetic role.[550]
 Beauty pageant festivals inside Iran were not held after the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_revolution"] 1979 revolution, and the last selection ceremony of the "beauty
queen of Iran" was held in 1978 in this country. Since then, many Iranian girls have participated in the Beauty pageant and
Miss Universe outside of Iran. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sahar_Biniaz"] Sahar Biniaz ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miss_Universe_Canada_2012"] Miss Universe Canada 2012) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shermine_Shahrivar"] Shermineh Shahrivar ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miss_Germany"] Miss Germany and
 Miss Europe) are examples of Iranian models outside Iran.[551][552] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Girls_of_Enghelab_Street"] Girls of Enghelab Street was a series of protests in
2017–2019 against a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijab_by_country#Iran"] compulsory hijab in Iran.[553]

Explanatory notes
a. Persian: ‎ایران ‎اسلامی ‎جمهوری Jomhuri-ye Eslāmi-ye Irān (  listen) [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian"] [dʒomhuːˌɾije eslɒːˌmije ʔiːˈɾɒn]
b. In the Avesta, the airiia- are members of the ethnic group of the Avesta-reciters themselves, in
contradistinction to the anairiia- (the "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aneran"] non-Arya"). The word also appears four times in Old Persian: One is
in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behistun_Inscription"] Behistun Inscription, where ariya- is the name of a language (DB 4.89). The other three instances
occur in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darius_the_Great"] Darius the Great's inscription at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naqsh-e_Rostam"] Naqsh-e Rostam (DNa 14–15), in Darius I's inscription at Susa
(DSe 13–14), and in the inscription of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xerxes_I"] Xerxes I at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persepolis"] Persepolis (XPh 12–13). In these, the two Achaemenid
dynasties describe themselves as pārsa pārsahyā puça ariya ariyaciça "a Persian, son of a Persian, an
Ariya, of Ariya origin."—The phrase with ciça ("origin, descendance") assures that ariya is an ethnic name
wider in meaning than pārsa and not a simple adjectival epithet.[39]

299. [URL: "https://web.archive.org/web/20170517002547/https://freedomhouse.org/report/freedom-world/2017/iran"] Freedom House (2017). "Iran" (https://web.archive.org/web/20170517002547/https://freedomhouse.org/rep
 ort/freedom-world/2017/iran). Freedom in the World 2017. Freedom House. Archived from the original (http
s://freedomhouse.org/report/freedom-world/2017/iran) on 17 May 2017. Retrieved 25 May 2017. "The
Islamic Republic of Iran holds elections regularly, but they fall short of democratic standards due to the role
of the hard-line Guardian Council, which disqualifies all candidates deemed insufficiently loyal to the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei"] clerical establishment. Ultimate power rests in the hands of the country's supreme leader, Ayatollah Ali
Khamenei, and the unelected institutions under his control. Human rights abuses continued unabated in
2016, with the authorities carrying out Iran's largest mass execution in years and launching a renewed
crackdown on women's rights activists. The regime maintained restrictions on freedom of expression, both
offline and online, and made further arrests of journalists, bloggers, labor union activists, and dual nationals
visiting the country, with some facing heavy prison sentences. Hard-liners controlling powerful institutions,
including the judiciary and the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC), were behind many of the year's
abuses. There were no indications that President Hassan Rouhani, a self-proclaimed moderate seeking
reelection in 2017, was willing or able to push back against repressive forces and deliver the greater social
freedoms he had promised. Opposition leaders Mir Hossein Mousavi, his wife Zahra Rahnavard, and
reformist cleric Mehdi Karroubi remained under house arrest for a sixth year without being formally charged
or put on trial. As in 2015, the media were barred from quoting or reporting on former president Mohammad
Khatami, another important reformist figure."
